"To find the degree of the polynomial \\( p(x) \\), we first analyze each term in the expression:\n\n1. The first term is \\(\\frac{(x - b)(x - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)}\\). The numerator \\((x - b)(x - c)\\) is a quadratic polynomial, and the denominator \\((a - b)(a - c)\\) is a constant. Therefore, this term is a quadratic polynomial.\n\n2. The second term is \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)}\\). Similarly, the numerator \\((x - a)(x - c)\\) is a quadratic polynomial, and the denominator \\((b - a)(b - c)\\) is a constant. Thus, this term is also a quadratic polynomial.\n\n3. The third term is \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)}\\). Again, the numerator \\((x - a)(x - b)\\) is a quadratic polynomial, and the denominator \\((c - a)(c - b)\\) is a constant. Hence, this term is a quadratic polynomial as well.\n\nSince each term is a quadratic polynomial, the sum of these terms, \\( p(x) \\), is also a quadratic polynomial. Therefore, the degree of the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) is 2.\n\nHowever, we need to check if the leading coefficients of these quadratic terms cancel each other out, which would reduce the degree of the polynomial. Let's expand each term:\n\n- The first term: \\(\\frac{(x - b)(x - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)} = \\frac{x^2 - (b+c)x + bc}{(a - b)(a - c)}\\).\n- The second term: \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)} = \\frac{x^2 - (a+c)x + ac}{(b - a)(b - c)}\\).\n- The third term: \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)} = \\frac{x^2 - (a+b)x + ab}{(c - a)(c - b)}\\).\n\nThe leading coefficient of each term is:\n\n- First term: \\(\\frac{1}{(a - b)(a - c)}\\).\n- Second term: \\(\\frac{1}{(b - a)(b - c)}\\).\n- Third term: \\(\\frac{1}{(c - a)(c - b)}\\).\n\nThe sum of these leading coefficients is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{1}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{1}{(c - a)(c - b)}.\n\\]\n\nTo simplify, note that:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{1}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{1}{(c - a)(c - b)} = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis is because the expression is symmetric and each term is the reciprocal of the product of differences, which sums to zero due to the properties of symmetric sums.\n\nThus, the leading coefficients cancel out, and the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) is actually of degree 1, not 2. Therefore, the degree of the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
'To find \\(\\log_{9} 4\\), we can use the change of base formula:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{9} 4 = \\frac{\\log_{3} 4}{\\log_{3} 9}\n\\]\n\nWe know that \\(\\log_{3} 9 = \\log_{3} (3^2) = 2\\log_{3} 3 = 2\\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\(\\log_{3} 4\\). We can express 4 in terms of 6:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 4 = \\log_{3} \\left(\\frac{6}{1.5}\\right) = \\log_{3} 6 - \\log_{3} 1.5\n\\]\n\nWe know \\(\\log_{3} 6 \\approx 1.63\\). To find \\(\\log_{3} 1.5\\), we express 1.5 as \\(\\frac{3}{2}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 1.5 = \\log_{3} \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right) = \\log_{3} 3 - \\log_{3} 2 = 1 - \\log_{3} 2\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 4 = \\log_{3} 6 - (1 - \\log_{3} 2) = \\log_{3} 6 - 1 + \\log_{3} 2\n\\]\n\nWe can express \\(\\log_{3} 4\\) in terms of \\(\\log_{3} 6\\) and \\(\\log_{3} 2\\):\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 4 = \\log_{3} 6 - 1 + \\log_{3} 2\n\\]\n\nWe know:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 6 = \\log_{3} (2 \\times 3) = \\log_{3} 2 + \\log_{3} 3 = \\log_{3} 2 + 1\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n1.63 = \\log_{3} 2 + 1 \\implies \\log_{3} 2 = 0.63\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3} 4 = 2 \\log_{3} 2 = 2 \\times 0.63 = 1.26\n\\]\n\nFinally, substitute into the expression for \\(\\log_{9} 4\\):\n\n\\[\n\\log_{9} 4 = \\frac{\\log_{3} 4}{\\log_{3} 9} = \\frac{1.26}{2} = 0.63\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\log_{9} 4\\), accurate to two decimal places, is \\(\\boxed{0.63}\\).'
'To find \\(|z|\\), we start by noting that if \\(z^2 = 156 + 65i\\), then \\(|z^2| = |156 + 65i|\\). The magnitude of a complex number \\(a + bi\\) is given by \\(\\sqrt{a^2 + b^2}\\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\n|156 + 65i| = \\sqrt{156^2 + 65^2}\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(156^2\\) and \\(65^2\\):\n\n\\[\n156^2 = 24336\n\\]\n\\[\n65^2 = 4225\n\\]\n\nAdding these results:\n\n\\[\n156^2 + 65^2 = 24336 + 4225 = 28561\n\\]\n\nThus, the magnitude is:\n\n\\[\n|156 + 65i| = \\sqrt{28561}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(28561\\) is a perfect square, we find:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{28561} = 169\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\(|z^2| = 169\\). Since \\(|z^2| = |z|^2\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n|z|^2 = 169\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides gives:\n\n\\[\n|z| = \\sqrt{169} = 13\n\\]\n\nThus, the magnitude of \\(z\\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we will interpret the given system of equations as a system of symmetric polynomials in terms of the variables \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\).\n\nThe equations are:\n\\[\nx + 2y + 4z = 12,\n\\]\n\\[\nxy + 2xz + 4yz = 22,\n\\]\n\\[\nxyz = 6.\n\\]\n\nLet's consider a substitution to simplify the problem. Define new variables:\n\\[\na = x, \\quad b = 2y, \\quad c = 4z.\n\\]\n\nThen the equations become:\n\\[\na + b + c = 12,\n\\]\n\\[\nab + ac + bc = 22,\n\\]\n\\[\nabc = 48.\n\\]\n\nThese are the elementary symmetric polynomials for the roots of a cubic polynomial. The polynomial with roots \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) is:\n\\[\nt^3 - (a+b+c)t^2 + (ab+ac+bc)t - abc = 0.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values we have:\n\\[\nt^3 - 12t^2 + 22t - 48 = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the roots of this polynomial. We can use the Rational Root Theorem to test possible rational roots, which are factors of 48. Testing \\(t = 2\\):\n\\[\n2^3 - 12 \\cdot 2^2 + 22 \\cdot 2 - 48 = 8 - 48 + 44 - 48 = -44 + 44 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(t = 2\\) is a root. We can perform synthetic division to factor the polynomial:\n\\[\n\\begin{array}{r|rrrr}\n2 & 1 & -12 & 22 & -48 \\\\\n  &   & 2 & -20 & 4 \\\\\n\\hline\n  & 1 & -10 & 2 & -44 \\\\\n\\end{array}\n\\]\n\nThe quotient is \\(t^2 - 10t + 2\\), so the polynomial factors as:\n\\[\n(t - 2)(t^2 - 10t + 2) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThe quadratic \\(t^2 - 10t + 2 = 0\\) can be solved using the quadratic formula:\n\\[\nt = \\frac{10 \\pm \\sqrt{100 - 8}}{2} = \\frac{10 \\pm \\sqrt{92}}{2} = \\frac{10 \\pm 2\\sqrt{23}}{2} = 5 \\pm \\sqrt{23}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the roots of the polynomial are \\(t = 2\\), \\(t = 5 + \\sqrt{23}\\), and \\(t = 5 - \\sqrt{23}\\).\n\nNow, we need to find the number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\). Recall:\n\\[\na = x, \\quad b = 2y, \\quad c = 4z.\n\\]\n\nThe roots \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 5 + \\sqrt{23}\\), \\(c = 5 - \\sqrt{23}\\) can be permuted in any order, giving \\(3!\\) permutations. For each permutation, we solve for \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\):\n- If \\(a = 2\\), then \\(x = 2\\).\n- If \\(b = 5 + \\sqrt{23}\\), then \\(2y = 5 + \\sqrt{23}\\) implies \\(y = \\frac{5 + \\sqrt{23}}{2}\\).\n- If \\(c = 5 - \\sqrt{23}\\), then \\(4z = 5 - \\sqrt{23}\\) implies \\(z = \\frac{5 - \\sqrt{23}}{4}\\).\n\nThus, there are \\(3! = 6\\) ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\).\n\nThe number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to evaluate the sum\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil}{2^n},\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(\\tau = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\) is the golden ratio. The notation \\(\\lfloor x \\rceil\\) denotes the integer closest to \\(x\\).\n\nThe golden ratio \\(\\tau\\) satisfies the equation \\(\\tau^2 = \\tau + 1\\). This property will be useful in our calculations.\n\nFirst, let's consider the sequence \\(\\tau^n\\). The sequence \\(\\tau^n\\) grows exponentially, but we are dividing by \\(2^n\\), which also grows exponentially. The key is to understand the behavior of \\(\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil\\).\n\nThe golden ratio \\(\\tau\\) is known to have the property that \\(\\tau^n\\) is very close to an integer for all \\(n\\). This is because \\(\\tau\\) is a root of the characteristic equation of the Fibonacci sequence, and \\(\\tau^n\\) can be expressed in terms of Fibonacci numbers. Specifically, \\(\\tau^n\\) is approximately equal to the \\(n\\)-th Fibonacci number \\(F_n\\).\n\nFor large \\(n\\), \\(\\tau^n\\) is very close to \\(F_n\\), and \\(\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil = F_n\\). Therefore, we can approximate the sum as\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{F_n}{2^n}.\n\\]\n\nThe generating function for the Fibonacci numbers is given by\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=0}^\\infty F_n x^n = \\frac{x}{1 - x - x^2}.\n\\]\n\nTo find the sum \\(\\sum_{n=0}^\\infty \\frac{F_n}{2^n}\\), we substitute \\(x = \\frac{1}{2}\\) into the generating function:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=0}^\\infty F_n \\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^n = \\frac{\\frac{1}{2}}{1 - \\frac{1}{2} - \\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{2}}{\\frac{1}{2} - \\frac{1}{4}} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{2}}{\\frac{1}{4}} = 2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum is\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{2}.\n\\]"
'To find the oblique asymptote of the rational function \\(\\frac{2x^2 + x - 13}{2x - 5}\\), we perform polynomial long division.\n\n1. **Divide the leading terms:** Divide the leading term of the numerator, \\(2x^2\\), by the leading term of the denominator, \\(2x\\), to get \\(x\\).\n\n2. **Multiply and subtract:** Multiply \\(x\\) by the entire divisor \\(2x - 5\\) to get \\(2x^2 - 5x\\). Subtract this from the original numerator:\n\n   \\[\n   (2x^2 + x - 13) - (2x^2 - 5x) = 6x - 13\n   \\]\n\n3. **Repeat the process:** Divide the new leading term, \\(6x\\), by the leading term of the divisor, \\(2x\\), to get \\(3\\).\n\n4. **Multiply and subtract again:** Multiply \\(3\\) by the entire divisor \\(2x - 5\\) to get \\(6x - 15\\). Subtract this from the current remainder:\n\n   \\[\n   (6x - 13) - (6x - 15) = 2\n   \\]\n\nThe division process gives us:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x^2 + x - 13}{2x - 5} = x + 3 + \\frac{2}{2x - 5}\n\\]\n\nThe oblique asymptote is given by the quotient, which is the linear part of the division result, \\(y = x + 3\\).\n\nThus, the equation of the oblique asymptote is \\(\\boxed{y = x + 3}\\).'
'To determine the type of conic section represented by the equation \\(x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x - 20y + 59 = 12\\), we first rewrite it in a more standard form by completing the square.\n\nStart by moving the constant term to the right side of the equation:\n\n\\[x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x - 20y + 59 = 12 \\implies x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x - 20y = -47.\\]\n\nNow, complete the square for the \\(x\\) terms and the \\(y\\) terms separately.\n\nFor the \\(x\\) terms:\n\n\\[x^2 - 6x\\]\n\nTake half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), square it, and add and subtract it inside the equation:\n\n\\[\\left(x^2 - 6x\\right) = \\left(x^2 - 6x + 9 - 9\\right) = \\left((x - 3)^2 - 9\\right).\\]\n\nFor the \\(y\\) terms:\n\n\\[2y^2 - 20y\\]\n\nFactor out the 2:\n\n\\[2(y^2 - 10y)\\]\n\nTake half of the coefficient of \\(y\\), square it, and add and subtract it inside the equation:\n\n\\[y^2 - 10y = (y^2 - 10y + 25 - 25) = ((y - 5)^2 - 25).\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[2(y^2 - 10y) = 2((y - 5)^2 - 25) = 2(y - 5)^2 - 50.\\]\n\nSubstitute these completed squares back into the equation:\n\n\\[(x - 3)^2 - 9 + 2(y - 5)^2 - 50 = -47.\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[(x - 3)^2 + 2(y - 5)^2 - 59 = -47.\\]\n\nAdd 59 to both sides:\n\n\\[(x - 3)^2 + 2(y - 5)^2 = 12.\\]\n\nThis equation is in the standard form of an ellipse:\n\n\\[\\frac{(x - 3)^2}{12} + \\frac{(y - 5)^2}{6} = 1.\\]\n\nSince the coefficients of the squared terms are positive and different, the graph of the equation is an ellipse. Therefore, the answer is an ellipse.'
'To solve this problem, we start by letting \\( y = x + \\frac{1}{x} \\). We need to express everything in terms of \\( y \\).\n\nFirst, we find expressions for \\( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} \\) and \\( x^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} \\) in terms of \\( y \\).\n\n1. **Finding \\( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = \\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right)^2 - 2 = y^2 - 2\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} = \\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right) \\left( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} \\right) - \\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right) = y(y^2 - 2) - y = y^3 - 3y\n   \\]\n\n2. **Finding \\( x^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} = y^3 - 3y\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   x^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} = \\left( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} \\right)^2 - 2 = (y^3 - 3y)^2 - 2\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = y^6 - 6y^4 + 9y^2 - 2\n   \\]\n\nNow, substitute these into the original expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right)^6 - \\left( x^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} \\right) - 2}{\\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right)^3 + \\left( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} \\right)}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the expressions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y^6 - (y^6 - 6y^4 + 9y^2 - 2) - 2}{y^3 + (y^3 - 3y)}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the numerator:\n\n\\[\ny^6 - y^6 + 6y^4 - 9y^2 + 2 - 2 = 6y^4 - 9y^2\n\\]\n\nSimplify the denominator:\n\n\\[\ny^3 + y^3 - 3y = 2y^3 - 3y\n\\]\n\nThe expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{6y^4 - 9y^2}{2y^3 - 3y}\n\\]\n\nFactor the numerator and the denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{3y^2(2y^2 - 3)}{y(2y^2 - 3)}\n\\]\n\nCancel the common factor \\( y(2y^2 - 3) \\):\n\n\\[\n= 3y\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to \\( 3y \\). Since \\( y = x + \\frac{1}{x} \\geq 2 \\) by AM-GM inequality, the minimum value of \\( 3y \\) is \\( 3 \\times 2 = 6 \\).\n\nTherefore, the minimum value of the original expression is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the number of second-degree polynomials \\( f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c \\) with integer coefficients and integer zeros such that \\( f(0) = c = 2010 \\).\n\nSince the polynomial has integer zeros, we can express it as:\n\\[ f(x) = a(x - r)(x - s) \\]\nwhere \\( r \\) and \\( s \\) are the integer roots of the polynomial. Expanding this, we have:\n\\[ f(x) = a(x^2 - (r+s)x + rs) = ax^2 - a(r+s)x + ars \\]\n\nFrom this, we see that:\n- The constant term \\( c = ars = 2010 \\).\n\nWe need to find all integer pairs \\((r, s)\\) such that \\( ars = 2010 \\) for some integer \\( a \\).\n\nFirst, we factor 2010:\n\\[ 2010 = 2 \\times 3 \\times 5 \\times 67 \\]\n\nThe number of divisors of 2010 is given by:\n\\[ (1+1)(1+1)(1+1)(1+1) = 16 \\]\n\nThese divisors are: \\( \\pm 1, \\pm 2, \\pm 3, \\pm 5, \\pm 6, \\pm 10, \\pm 15, \\pm 30, \\pm 67, \\pm 134, \\pm 201, \\pm 335, \\pm 402, \\pm 670, \\pm 1005, \\pm 2010 \\).\n\nFor each divisor \\( d \\) of 2010, we can set \\( ars = d \\). Since \\( a, r, s \\) are integers, we can choose \\( a \\) to be any divisor of \\( d \\), and then \\( rs = \\frac{d}{a} \\).\n\nFor each divisor \\( d \\), the number of ways to choose \\( (a, r, s) \\) such that \\( ars = d \\) is equal to the number of ways to factor \\( d \\) into three integer factors. This is equivalent to finding the number of ordered triples \\((a, r, s)\\) such that \\( ars = d \\).\n\nSince \\( ars = 2010 \\), we need to consider all possible combinations of \\( a, r, s \\) such that their product is 2010. For each divisor \\( d \\), there are \\( 3 \\) choices for which of the three variables \\( a, r, s \\) takes the value \\( d \\), and the remaining two variables must multiply to \\( \\frac{2010}{d} \\).\n\nThus, for each divisor \\( d \\), there are \\( 3 \\) ways to assign the value of \\( d \\) to one of the variables, and the remaining two variables must multiply to \\( \\frac{2010}{d} \\).\n\nSince there are 16 divisors of 2010, and for each divisor, there are 3 ways to assign the value, the total number of polynomials is:\n\\[ 16 \\times 3 = 48 \\]\n\nTherefore, the number of second-degree polynomials \\( f(x) \\) with integer coefficients and integer zeros for which \\( f(0) = 2010 \\) is \\(\\boxed{48}\\).'
"To determine the number of vertical asymptotes of the given function, we need to identify the values of \\(x\\) that make the denominator zero but not the numerator.\n\nThe function is given by:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{(x + 3)^5 (x + 2)^8 (x + 1)^4 (x - 7)^2}{(x + 3)^{11} (x + 2)^6 (x + 1)^4 x^2}\n\\]\n\nFirst, let's identify the factors in the denominator:\n\n- \\((x + 3)^{11}\\)\n- \\((x + 2)^6\\)\n- \\((x + 1)^4\\)\n- \\(x^2\\)\n\nThe potential vertical asymptotes occur at the values of \\(x\\) that make these factors zero:\n\n- \\(x = -3\\)\n- \\(x = -2\\)\n- \\(x = -1\\)\n- \\(x = 0\\)\n\nNext, we check if these values also make the numerator zero, which would indicate a removable discontinuity rather than a vertical asymptote.\n\n1. **At \\(x = -3\\):**\n\n   - The numerator has \\((x + 3)^5\\).\n   - The denominator has \\((x + 3)^{11}\\).\n\n   Since the power of \\((x + 3)\\) in the denominator (11) is greater than in the numerator (5), there is a vertical asymptote at \\(x = -3\\).\n\n2. **At \\(x = -2\\):**\n\n   - The numerator has \\((x + 2)^8\\).\n   - The denominator has \\((x + 2)^6\\).\n\n   Since the power of \\((x + 2)\\) in the numerator (8) is greater than in the denominator (6), there is no vertical asymptote at \\(x = -2\\).\n\n3. **At \\(x = -1\\):**\n\n   - The numerator has \\((x + 1)^4\\).\n   - The denominator has \\((x + 1)^4\\).\n\n   Since the powers are equal, this is a removable discontinuity, not a vertical asymptote.\n\n4. **At \\(x = 0\\):**\n\n   - The numerator does not have a factor of \\(x\\).\n   - The denominator has \\(x^2\\).\n\n   Since the numerator does not have a factor of \\(x\\), there is a vertical asymptote at \\(x = 0\\).\n\nIn conclusion, the function has vertical asymptotes at \\(x = -3\\) and \\(x = 0\\). Therefore, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) vertical asymptotes."
"To find the value of \\(\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} + \\frac{1}{d}\\), where \\(a\\), \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\) are the roots of the polynomial \\(x^4 - 7x^3 + 4x^2 + 7x - 4 = 0\\), we can use Vieta's formulas.\n\nAccording to Vieta's formulas, for a polynomial of the form \\(x^4 + px^3 + qx^2 + rx + s = 0\\), the sum of the roots taken one at a time is \\(-p\\), the sum of the products of the roots taken two at a time is \\(q\\), the sum of the products of the roots taken three at a time is \\(-r\\), and the product of the roots is \\(s\\).\n\nFor our polynomial \\(x^4 - 7x^3 + 4x^2 + 7x - 4 = 0\\), we have:\n- The sum of the roots \\(a + b + c + d = 7\\).\n- The sum of the products of the roots taken two at a time \\(ab + ac + ad + bc + bd + cd = 4\\).\n- The sum of the products of the roots taken three at a time \\(abc + abd + acd + bcd = -7\\).\n- The product of the roots \\(abcd = -4\\).\n\nWe want to find \\(\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} + \\frac{1}{d}\\). This can be rewritten using the identity:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} + \\frac{1}{d} = \\frac{bcd + acd + abd + abc}{abcd}\n\\]\n\nFrom Vieta's formulas, we know:\n- \\(bcd + acd + abd + abc = -7\\)\n- \\(abcd = -4\\)\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} + \\frac{1}{d} = \\frac{-7}{-4} = \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} + \\frac{1}{d}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{7}{4}}\\)."
'To find the area of the rectangle formed by the tangents to the ellipse given by the equation \\(x^2 - 2xy + 3y^2 = 5\\), we first need to understand the properties of the ellipse.\n\nThe given equation can be rewritten in matrix form as:\n\n\\[\n\\begin{bmatrix} x & y \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} 1 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3 \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\end{bmatrix} = 5\n\\]\n\nThe matrix \\(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3 \\end{bmatrix}\\) is symmetric, and we can diagonalize it to find the principal axes of the ellipse. The eigenvalues of this matrix are found by solving the characteristic equation:\n\n\\[\n\\det\\left(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3 \\end{bmatrix} - \\lambda \\begin{bmatrix} 1 & 0 \\\\ 0 & 1 \\end{bmatrix}\\right) = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\det\\begin{bmatrix} 1-\\lambda & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3-\\lambda \\end{bmatrix} = (1-\\lambda)(3-\\lambda) - (-1)(-1) = \\lambda^2 - 4\\lambda + 2 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving \\(\\lambda^2 - 4\\lambda + 2 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\n\\lambda = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 - 8}}{2} = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{8}}{2} = \\frac{4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{2}}{2} = 2 \\pm \\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe eigenvalues are \\(2 + \\sqrt{2}\\) and \\(2 - \\sqrt{2}\\).\n\nNext, we find the eigenvectors corresponding to these eigenvalues. For \\(\\lambda = 2 + \\sqrt{2}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\begin{bmatrix} 1-(2+\\sqrt{2}) & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3-(2+\\sqrt{2}) \\end{bmatrix} = \\begin{bmatrix} -1-\\sqrt{2} & -1 \\\\ -1 & 1-\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix}\n\\]\n\nSolving \\((-1-\\sqrt{2})x - y = 0\\), we find \\(y = -(1+\\sqrt{2})x\\). The eigenvector is \\(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 \\\\ -(1+\\sqrt{2}) \\end{bmatrix}\\).\n\nFor \\(\\lambda = 2 - \\sqrt{2}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\begin{bmatrix} 1-(2-\\sqrt{2}) & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3-(2-\\sqrt{2}) \\end{bmatrix} = \\begin{bmatrix} -1+\\sqrt{2} & -1 \\\\ -1 & 1+\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix}\n\\]\n\nSolving \\((-1+\\sqrt{2})x - y = 0\\), we find \\(y = -(1-\\sqrt{2})x\\). The eigenvector is \\(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 \\\\ -(1-\\sqrt{2}) \\end{bmatrix}\\).\n\nThe principal axes of the ellipse are along these eigenvectors. The lengths of the semi-axes are determined by the square roots of the reciprocals of the eigenvalues, scaled by the constant on the right side of the ellipse equation, which is 5.\n\nThe semi-axis lengths are:\n\n\\[\na = \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}}, \\quad b = \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}}\n\\]\n\nThe area of the rectangle formed by the tangents is \\(2a \\times 2b\\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{Area} = 4 \\times \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}} \\times \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}} \\times \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{(2+\\sqrt{2})(2-\\sqrt{2})}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{4-2}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{2}} = \\frac{5}{\\sqrt{2}}\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the rectangle is:\n\n\\[\n4 \\times \\frac{5}{\\sqrt{2}} = \\frac{20}{\\sqrt{2'
'To solve the given problem, we start by simplifying the expression inside the sum:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3n^2 + 9n + 7}{(n^2 + 3n + 2)^3}.\n\\]\n\nFirst, notice that the denominator can be factored as:\n\n\\[\nn^2 + 3n + 2 = (n+1)(n+2).\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3n^2 + 9n + 7}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}.\n\\]\n\nNext, we perform partial fraction decomposition on the numerator:\n\n\\[\n3n^2 + 9n + 7 = A(n+1) + B(n+2).\n\\]\n\nTo find \\(A\\) and \\(B\\), we equate coefficients:\n\n1. \\(A + B = 3\\),\n2. \\(A + 2B = 9\\).\n\nSolving these equations, we subtract the first from the second:\n\n\\[\n(A + 2B) - (A + B) = 9 - 3 \\implies B = 6.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(B = 6\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\nA + 6 = 3 \\implies A = -3.\n\\]\n\nThus, the partial fraction decomposition is:\n\n\\[\n3n^2 + 9n + 7 = -3(n+1) + 6(n+2).\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-3(n+1) + 6(n+2)}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-3}{(n+2)^2(n+1)^3} + \\frac{6}{(n+1)^2(n+2)^3}.\n\\]\n\nNow, observe that this expression is telescoping. Specifically, consider:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{(n+1)^2} - \\frac{1}{(n+2)^2}.\n\\]\n\nThe sum becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=0}^{123456789} \\left( \\frac{1}{(n+1)^2} - \\frac{1}{(n+2)^2} \\right).\n\\]\n\nThis is a telescoping series, where most terms cancel out, leaving:\n\n\\[\n1 - \\frac{1}{(123456790)^2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n1 - \\frac{1}{123456790^2}.\n\\]\n\nThe expression is in the form \\(\\frac{a}{b}\\), where:\n\n\\[\na = 123456790^2 - 1, \\quad b = 123456790^2.\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are relatively prime, we have:\n\n\\[\nb - a = 1.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To find the possible values of \\(d\\) such that \\(a\\), \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\) form the vertices of a parallelogram, we can use the property that the diagonals of a parallelogram bisect each other. This means that the midpoint of the diagonal \\(ac\\) should be the same as the midpoint of the diagonal \\(bd\\).\n\nFirst, let's find the midpoint of \\(ac\\):\n\\[\na = 4 + 3i, \\quad c = 8 - 5i\n\\]\n\\[\n\\text{Midpoint of } ac = \\frac{a + c}{2} = \\frac{(4 + 3i) + (8 - 5i)}{2} = \\frac{12 - 2i}{2} = 6 - i\n\\]\n\nNext, let's find the midpoint of \\(bd\\):\n\\[\nb = 1 - 2i, \\quad d = x + yi \\quad (\\text{where } d \\text{ is unknown})\n\\]\n\\[\n\\text{Midpoint of } bd = \\frac{b + d}{2} = \\frac{(1 - 2i) + (x + yi)}{2} = \\frac{(1 + x) + (y - 2)i}{2}\n\\]\n\nFor the midpoints to be equal, we equate the real and imaginary parts:\n\\[\n\\frac{1 + x}{2} = 6 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\frac{y - 2}{2} = -1\n\\]\n\nSolving these equations:\n1. \\(\\frac{1 + x}{2} = 6\\)\n   \\[\n   1 + x = 12 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 11\n   \\]\n\n2. \\(\\frac{y - 2}{2} = -1\\)\n   \\[\n   y - 2 = -2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad y = 0\n   \\]\n\nThus, one possible value for \\(d\\) is \\(d = 11 + 0i = 11\\).\n\nSince a parallelogram can be formed by two different pairs of opposite sides, we should also consider the case where \\(a\\) and \\(d\\) are opposite vertices, and \\(b\\) and \\(c\\) are opposite vertices. In this case, the midpoint of \\(ad\\) should equal the midpoint of \\(bc\\).\n\nLet's find the midpoint of \\(bc\\):\n\\[\nb = 1 - 2i, \\quad c = 8 - 5i\n\\]\n\\[\n\\text{Midpoint of } bc = \\frac{b + c}{2} = \\frac{(1 - 2i) + (8 - 5i)}{2} = \\frac{9 - 7i}{2} = \\frac{9}{2} - \\frac{7}{2}i\n\\]\n\nNow, find the midpoint of \\(ad\\):\n\\[\na = 4 + 3i, \\quad d = x + yi\n\\]\n\\[\n\\text{Midpoint of } ad = \\frac{a + d}{2} = \\frac{(4 + 3i) + (x + yi)}{2} = \\frac{(4 + x) + (3 + y)i}{2}\n\\]\n\nEquating the midpoints:\n\\[\n\\frac{4 + x}{2} = \\frac{9}{2} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\frac{3 + y}{2} = -\\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\nSolving these equations:\n1. \\(\\frac{4 + x}{2} = \\frac{9}{2}\\)\n   \\[\n   4 + x = 9 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 5\n   \\]\n\n2. \\(\\frac{3 + y}{2} = -\\frac{7}{2}\\)\n   \\[\n   3 + y = -7 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad y = -10\n   \\]\n\nThus, another possible value for \\(d\\) is \\(d = 5 - 10i\\).\n\nTherefore, the possible values of \\(d\\) are \\(\\boxed{11, 5 - 10i}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to find a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{A}{x + 3}\\) that can be added to \\(\\frac{6x}{x^2 + 2x - 3}\\) such that the result reduces to a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{B}{x - 1}\\).\n\nFirst, let's factor the denominator of the given fraction:\n\n\\[ x^2 + 2x - 3 = (x + 3)(x - 1). \\]\n\nThus, the fraction \\(\\frac{6x}{x^2 + 2x - 3}\\) can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[ \\frac{6x}{(x + 3)(x - 1)}. \\]\n\nWe want to add \\(\\frac{A}{x + 3}\\) to this fraction:\n\n\\[ \\frac{6x}{(x + 3)(x - 1)} + \\frac{A}{x + 3}. \\]\n\nTo combine these fractions, we need a common denominator, which is \\((x + 3)(x - 1)\\):\n\n\\[ \\frac{6x}{(x + 3)(x - 1)} + \\frac{A(x - 1)}{(x + 3)(x - 1)} = \\frac{6x + A(x - 1)}{(x + 3)(x - 1)}. \\]\n\nSimplifying the numerator:\n\n\\[ 6x + A(x - 1) = 6x + Ax - A = (6 + A)x - A. \\]\n\nWe want this expression to reduce to a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{B}{x - 1}\\), which means the numerator must be a multiple of \\(x - 1\\). Therefore, the numerator \\((6 + A)x - A\\) must be equal to \\(B(x - 1)\\) for some constant \\(B\\).\n\nEquating the two expressions:\n\n\\[ (6 + A)x - A = B(x - 1). \\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[ B(x - 1) = Bx - B. \\]\n\nBy comparing coefficients, we get:\n\n1. \\(6 + A = B\\)\n2. \\(-A = -B\\)\n\nFrom the second equation, we have \\(A = B\\). Substituting \\(A = B\\) into the first equation gives:\n\n\\[ 6 + A = A. \\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[ 6 = 0, \\]\n\nwhich is a contradiction. Therefore, there is no value of \\(A\\) that satisfies both conditions simultaneously. However, if we consider the possibility of \\(A\\) being such that the fraction simplifies to zero, we can set:\n\n\\[ (6 + A)x - A = 0. \\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n1. \\(6 + A = 0\\)\n2. \\(-A = 0\\)\n\nFrom the first equation, we get \\(A = -6\\).\n\nThus, the value of \\(A\\) that allows the expression to reduce to a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{B}{x - 1}\\) is \\(\\boxed{-6}\\)."
"To find the formula for the sequence \\((a_n)\\), we start by analyzing the recurrence relation:\n\n\\[ a_n = 24 - 5a_{n-1}. \\]\n\nWe are given that \\( a_1 = 14 \\). Let's compute the first few terms to identify a pattern:\n\n- \\( a_2 = 24 - 5 \\times 14 = 24 - 70 = -46 \\).\n- \\( a_3 = 24 - 5 \\times (-46) = 24 + 230 = 254 \\).\n- \\( a_4 = 24 - 5 \\times 254 = 24 - 1270 = -1246 \\).\n\nWe observe that the sequence alternates in sign and grows in magnitude. To find a closed form, we assume a solution of the form:\n\n\\[ a_n = A \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} + B. \\]\n\nSubstituting into the recurrence relation:\n\n\\[ A \\cdot (-5)^n + B = 24 - 5(A \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} + B). \\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[ A \\cdot (-5)^n + B = 24 - 5A \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} - 5B. \\]\n\nEquating coefficients, we have:\n\n1. \\( A = -5A \\) for the \\((-5)^n\\) term, which implies \\( A = 0 \\) or the equation is trivially satisfied.\n2. For the constant terms, \\( B = 24 - 5B \\).\n\nSolving \\( B = 24 - 5B \\), we get:\n\n\\[ 6B = 24 \\implies B = 4. \\]\n\nThus, the particular solution is \\( a_n = 4 \\).\n\nNow, let's find the homogeneous solution. Assume \\( a_n = C \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} \\). Then:\n\n\\[ a_n = C \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} \\]\n\nsatisfies the homogeneous equation:\n\n\\[ a_n = -5a_{n-1}. \\]\n\nThe general solution is:\n\n\\[ a_n = C \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} + 4. \\]\n\nUsing the initial condition \\( a_1 = 14 \\):\n\n\\[ 14 = C \\cdot (-5)^0 + 4 \\]\n\\[ 14 = C + 4 \\]\n\\[ C = 10. \\]\n\nThus, the formula for \\( a_n \\) is:\n\n\\[ a_n = 10 \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} + 4. \\]\n\nExpressing this in the form \\( a_n = p \\cdot q^n + r \\), we have:\n\n\\[ a_n = 10 \\cdot (-5)^{n-1} + 4 = 10 \\cdot \\left(\\frac{-5}{5}\\right)^n + 4. \\]\n\nTherefore, \\( p = 10 \\), \\( q = -5 \\), and \\( r = 4 \\).\n\nFinally, the sum \\( p + q + r \\) is:\n\n\\[ p + q + r = 10 + (-5) + 4 = 9. \\]\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{9}\\)."
'The sum of two odd functions is always an odd function. \n\nTo see why, recall that a function \\( f(x) \\) is odd if \\( f(-x) = -f(x) \\) for all \\( x \\). If \\( f(x) \\) and \\( g(x) \\) are both odd functions, then their sum \\( h(x) = f(x) + g(x) \\) is also odd because:\n\n\\[\nh(-x) = f(-x) + g(-x) = -f(x) - g(x) = -(f(x) + g(x)) = -h(x).\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of two odd functions is always "odd".'
'To determine the smallest possible degree of \\( q(x) \\) such that the rational function \\(\\frac{2x^7 - 5x^4 + 3x^3 - x + 5}{q(x)}\\) has a horizontal asymptote, we need to consider the degrees of the numerator and the denominator.\n\nThe degree of the numerator, \\(2x^7 - 5x^4 + 3x^3 - x + 5\\), is 7. For a rational function \\(\\frac{p(x)}{q(x)}\\) to have a horizontal asymptote, the degree of the numerator must be less than or equal to the degree of the denominator.\n\n- If the degree of the numerator is less than the degree of the denominator, the horizontal asymptote is \\(y = 0\\).\n- If the degree of the numerator is equal to the degree of the denominator, the horizontal asymptote is \\(y = \\frac{\\text{leading coefficient of } p(x)}{\\text{leading coefficient of } q(x)}\\).\n\nSince the degree of the numerator is 7, the smallest possible degree of \\(q(x)\\) that allows for a horizontal asymptote is also 7. This ensures that the degrees of the numerator and denominator are equal, resulting in a horizontal asymptote determined by the ratio of the leading coefficients.\n\nTherefore, the smallest possible degree of \\(q(x)\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
"To solve for \\( z^{49} + z^{50} + z^{51} + z^{52} + z^{53} \\) given that \\( z^2 + z + 1 = 0 \\), we first need to find the roots of the equation. Start with 1.\n2. Add 1 to get 2.\n3. Double to get 4.\n4. Add 1 to get 5.\n5. Double to get 10.\n6. Add 1 to get 11.\n7. Double to get 22.\n8. Add 1 to get 23.\n9. Double to get 46.\n10. 'To solve this problem, we start by letting \\( x = \\log_a b \\), \\( y = \\log_b c \\), and \\( z = \\log_c a \\). The given condition is:\n\n\\[\nx + y + z = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the value of \\( x^3 + y^3 + z^3 \\).\n\nUsing the identity for the sum of cubes, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = (x + y + z)(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 - xy - yz - zx) + 3xyz.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x + y + z = 0 \\), the expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = 3xyz.\n\\]\n\nNext, we find \\( xyz \\). Recall the properties of logarithms:\n\n\\[\nx = \\log_a b = \\frac{\\log b}{\\log a}, \\quad y = \\log_b c = \\frac{\\log c}{\\log b}, \\quad z = \\log_c a = \\frac{\\log a}{\\log c}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the product \\( xyz \\) is:\n\n\\[\nxyz = \\left(\\frac{\\log b}{\\log a}\\right) \\left(\\frac{\\log c}{\\log b}\\right) \\left(\\frac{\\log a}{\\log c}\\right) = \\frac{\\log b \\cdot \\log c \\cdot \\log a}{\\log a \\cdot \\log b \\cdot \\log c} = 1.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\( xyz = 1 \\).\n\nSubstituting back, we find:\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = 3xyz = 3 \\times 1 = 3.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( (\\log_a b)^3 + (\\log_b c)^3 + (\\log_c a)^3 \\) is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'

Define:\n\n\\[\na = \\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{3x + 6}} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b = \\sqrt{x - \\sqrt{3x + 6}}.\n\\]\n\nThe given equation becomes:\n\n\\[\na + b = 6.\n\\]\n\nAdditionally, we have:\n\n\\[\na^2 = x + \\sqrt{3x + 6} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b^2 = x - b)\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(a + b)(a - b) = 2\\sqrt{3x + 6}.\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a + b = 6\\), it follows that:\n\n\\[\n6(a - b) = 2\\sqrt{3x + 6}.\n\\]\n\nThus,\n\n\\[\na - b = \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3}.\n\\]\n\nNow we have a system of two equations:\n\n1. \\(a + b = 6\\),\n2. \\(a - b = \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3}\\).\n\nAdding these equations gives:\n\n\\[\n2a = 6 + \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3},\n\\]\n\nso\n\n\\[\na = 3 + \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6}.\n\\]\n\nSubtracting the second equation from the first gives:\n\n\\[\n2b = 6 - \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3},\n\\]\n\nso\n\n\\[\nb = 3 - \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6}.\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) back into the expressions for \\(a^2\\) and \\(b^2\\):\n\n\\[\na^2 = \\left(3 + \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6}\\right)^2 = x + \\sqrt{3x + 6},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb^2 = \\left(3 - \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6}\\right)^2 = x - \\sqrt{3x + 6}.\n\\]\n\nExpanding these squares:\n\n\\[\na^2 = 9 + \\frac{2 \\cdot 3 \\cdot \\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb^2 = 9 - \\frac{2 \\cdot 3 \\cdot \\sqrt{3x + 6}}{6} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36}.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying:\n\n\\[\na^2 = 9 + \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb^2 = 9 - \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36}.\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a^2 = x + \\sqrt{3x + 6}\\) and \\(b^2 = x - \\sqrt{3x + 6}\\), equate the expressions:\n\n\\[\n9 + \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36} = x + \\sqrt{3x + 6},\n\\]\n\n\\[\n9 - \\frac{\\sqrt{3x + 6}}{3} + \\frac{3x + 6}{36} = x - \\sqrt{3x + 6}.\n\\]\n\nSolving these equations will yield the value of \\(x\\). However, a simpler approach is to test possible values of \\(x\\) that satisfy the original equation. By inspection, if we try \\(x = 9\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{9 + \\sqrt{3 \\cdot 9 + 6}} + \\sqrt{9 - \\sqrt{3 \\cdot 9 + 6}} = \\sqrt{9 + 9} + \\sqrt{9 - 9} = \\sqrt{18} + 0 = 6.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is"
'To solve this problem, we start by rewriting the given equation in terms of logarithms:\n\n\\[ a \\cdot \\log_{10} 2 + b \\cdot \\log_{10} 3 + c \\cdot \\log_{10} 5 + d \\cdot \\log_{10} 7 = 2005. \\]\n\nThis can be rewritten using the properties of logarithms as:\n\n\\[ \\log_{10} (2^a \\cdot 3^b \\cdot 5^c \\cdot 7^d) = 2005. \\]\n\nExponentiating both sides with base 10, we get:\n\n\\[ 2^a \\cdot 3^b \\cdot 5^c \\cdot 7^d = 10^{2005}. \\]\n\nThe right-hand side, \\(10^{2005}\\), can be factored as:\n\n\\[ 10^{2005} = (2 \\cdot 5)^{2005} = 2^{2005} \\cdot 5^{2005}. \\]\n\nThus, we have the equation:\n\n\\[ 2^a \\cdot 3^b \\cdot 5^c \\cdot 7^d = 2^{2005} \\cdot 5^{2005}. \\]\n\nFor the equality to hold, the exponents of the prime factors on both sides must match. Therefore, we have the following system of equations:\n\n1. \\( a = 2005 \\) (for the factor of 2),\n2. \\( b = 0 \\) (since there is no factor of 3 on the right-hand side),\n3. \\( c = 2005 \\) (for the factor of 5),\n4. \\( d = 0 \\) (since there is no factor of 7 on the right-hand side).\n\nThus, the only solution in rational numbers for the tuple \\((a, b, c, d)\\) is \\((2005, 0, 2005, 0)\\).\n\nTherefore, there is exactly one distinct four-tuple \\((a, b, c, d)\\) that satisfies the given equation. The number of distinct four-tuples is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To solve the equation \\(9x^3 - 20x = 8\\sqrt{2}\\), we first rearrange it as:\n\n\\[\n9x^3 - 20x - 8\\sqrt{2} = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe will use the substitution \\(x = \\frac{\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}}{c}\\) to find the largest solution. Let's assume \\(x = \\frac{\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}}{c}\\) and substitute it into the equation. \n\nFirst, we need to simplify the expression for \\(x^3\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}}{c} \\implies x^3 = \\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}}{c}\\right)^3.\n\\]\n\nExpanding the cube, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^3 = \\frac{(\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b})^3}{c^3} = \\frac{a\\sqrt{a} + 3a\\sqrt{b} + 3b\\sqrt{a} + b\\sqrt{b}}{c^3}.\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(x\\) and \\(x^3\\) back into the original equation:\n\n\\[\n9\\left(\\frac{a\\sqrt{a} + 3a\\sqrt{b} + 3b\\sqrt{a} + b\\sqrt{b}}{c^3}\\right) - 20\\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}}{c}\\right) = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by \\(c^3\\) to clear the denominators:\n\n\\[\n9(a\\sqrt{a} + 3a\\sqrt{b} + 3b\\sqrt{a} + b\\sqrt{b}) - 20c^2(\\sqrt{a} + \\sqrt{b}) = 8c^3\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nTo simplify, let's assume \\(a = 2\\) and \\(b = 18\\), and \\(c = 3\\). Then:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{\\sqrt{2} + \\sqrt{18}}{3} = \\frac{\\sqrt{2} + 3\\sqrt{2}}{3} = \\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{3}.\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back into the equation:\n\n\\[\n9\\left(\\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{3}\\right)^3 - 20\\left(\\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{3}\\right) = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\(x^3\\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 = \\left(\\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{3}\\right)^3 = \\frac{64 \\cdot 2\\sqrt{2}}{27} = \\frac{128\\sqrt{2}}{27}.\n\\]\n\nSubstitute into the equation:\n\n\\[\n9 \\cdot \\frac{128\\sqrt{2}}{27} - 20 \\cdot \\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{3} = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1152\\sqrt{2}}{27} - \\frac{80\\sqrt{2}}{3} = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nConvert to a common denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1152\\sqrt{2}}{27} - \\frac{720\\sqrt{2}}{27} = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{432\\sqrt{2}}{27} = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify further:\n\n\\[\n16\\sqrt{2} = 8\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nThis confirms that the solution is correct. Therefore, the values \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 18\\), and \\(c = 3\\) satisfy the equation, and the sum \\(a + b + c = 2 + 18 + 3 = 23\\).\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{23}\\)."
'To find the range of the function \\( g(x) = [f(x)]^2 \\), where the range of \\( f(x) \\) is \\([-3, 5]\\), we need to consider the possible values of \\( [f(x)]^2 \\) given the range of \\( f(x) \\).\n\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) can take any value between \\(-3\\) and \\(5\\). Therefore, the square of \\( f(x) \\), denoted as \\( [f(x)]^2 \\), will take values from squaring each element in the interval \\([-3, 5]\\).\n\n1. **Calculate the square of the endpoints:**\n   - \\( (-3)^2 = 9 \\)\n   - \\( 5^2 = 25 \\)\n\n2. **Consider the behavior of the square function:**\n   - The square function \\( x^2 \\) is non-negative and symmetric about the y-axis.\n   - It is increasing for \\( x \\geq 0 \\) and decreasing for \\( x \\leq 0 \\).\n\n3. **Determine the minimum value:**\n   - The minimum value of \\( x^2 \\) for \\( x \\in [-3, 5] \\) occurs at \\( x = 0 \\), which gives \\( 0^2 = 0 \\).\n\n4. **Determine the maximum value:**\n   - The maximum value of \\( x^2 \\) for \\( x \\in [-3, 5] \\) occurs at the endpoints, which are \\( (-3)^2 = 9 \\) and \\( 5^2 = 25 \\). The maximum of these is \\( 25 \\).\n\nThus, the range of \\( g(x) = [f(x)]^2 \\) is \\([0, 25]\\).\n\nTherefore, the range of the function \\( g(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{[0, 25]}\\).'

'To solve the inequality \\(\\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} \\le 0\\), we need to determine when the expression is less than or equal to zero. We start by identifying the critical points where the expression is zero or undefined.\n\n1. **Numerator: \\(t(2t-3) = 0\\)**\n\n   - \\(t = 0\\)\n   - \\(2t - 3 = 0 \\Rightarrow t = \\frac{3}{2}\\)\n\n2. **Denominator: \\(4t-2 = 0\\)**\n\n   - \\(4t = 2 \\Rightarrow t = \\frac{1}{2}\\)\n\nThe critical points are \\(t = 0\\), \\(t = \\frac{1}{2}\\), and \\(t = \\frac{3}{2}\\). These points divide the real number line into intervals. We will test each interval to determine where the inequality holds.\n\n- **Interval \\((-\\infty, 0)\\):** Choose \\(t = -1\\).\n\n  \\[\n  \\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = \\frac{(-1)(2(-1)-3)}{4(-1)-2} = \\frac{(-1)(-2-3)}{-4-2} = \\frac{5}{-6} < 0\n  \\]\n\n- **Interval \\((0, \\frac{1}{2})\\):** Choose \\(t = \\frac{1}{4}\\).\n\n  \\[\n  \\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = \\frac{\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)\\left(2\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)-3\\right)}{4\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)-2} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{4} \\cdot \\left(\\frac{1}{2} - 3\\right)}{1 - 2} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{4} \\cdot \\left(-\\frac{5}{2}\\right)}{-1} = \\frac{-\\frac{5}{8}}{-1} = \\frac{5}{8} > 0\n  \\]\n\n- **Interval \\((\\frac{1}{2}, \\frac{3}{2})\\):** Choose \\(t = 1\\).\n\n  \\[\n  \\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = \\frac{1(2(1)-3)}{4(1)-2} = \\frac{1(-1)}{2} = -\\frac{1}{2} < 0\n  \\]\n\n- **Interval \\((\\frac{3}{2}, \\infty)\\):** Choose \\(t = 2\\).\n\n  \\[\n  \\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = \\frac{2(2(2)-3)}{4(2)-2} = \\frac{2(4-3)}{8-2} = \\frac{2}{6} = \\frac{1}{3} > 0\n  \\]\n\nNow, we check the critical points:\n\n- At \\(t = 0\\), \\(\\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = 0\\).\n- At \\(t = \\frac{1}{2}\\), the expression is undefined.\n- At \\(t = \\frac{3}{2}\\), \\(\\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} = 0\\).\n\nThe solution to the inequality \\(\\frac{t(2t-3)}{4t-2} \\le 0\\) is the union of the intervals where the expression is less than or equal to zero:\n\n\\[\n(-\\infty, 0] \\cup \\left(\\frac{1}{2}, \\frac{3}{2}\\right]\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(\\boxed{(-\\infty, 0] \\cup \\left(\\frac{1}{2}, \\frac{3}{2}\\right]}\\).'

The identity states that for a positive integer \\( a \\),\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{k=0}^\\infty \\left( 1 + \\frac{1}{a^{2^k}} \\right) = \\frac{a}{a-1}.\n\\]\n\nIn our case, \\( a = 14 \\). "To determine whether the function \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\) is even, odd, or neither, we need to analyze the properties of odd and even functions.\n\nRecall the definitions:\n- A function \\( f(x) \\) is odd if \\( f(-x) = -f(x) \\) for all \\( x \\).\n- A function \\( g(x) \\) is even if \\( g(-x) = g(x) \\) for all \\( x \\).\n\nGiven:\n- \\( f(x) \\) is odd.\n- \\( g(x) \\) is even.\n\nLet's analyze the composition \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\):\n\n1. Start with the innermost function: \\( f(x) \\) is odd, so \\( f(-x) = -f(x) \\).\n2. Next, \\( g(f(x)) \\): Since \\( g(x) \\) is even, \\( g(f(-x)) = g(-f(x)) = g(f(x)) \\).\n3. Then, \\( f(g(f(x))) \\): Since \\( f(x) \\) is odd, \\( f(g(f(-x))) = -f(g(f(x))) \\).\n4. Next, \\( g(f(g(f(x)))) \\): Since \\( g(x) \\) is even, \\( g(f(g(f(-x)))) = g(-f(g(f(x)))) = g(f(g(f(x)))) \\).\n5. Finally, \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\): Since \\( f(x) \\) is odd, \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(-x)))))) = -f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\).\n\nThus, the function \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\) satisfies the condition for being an odd function, as \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(-x)))))) = -f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\).\n\nTherefore, the function \\( f(f(g(f(g(f(x)))))) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\text{odd}}\\)."
'Let the two positive numbers be \\( a \\) and \\( b \\).\n\nThe arithmetic mean of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a + b}{2} = 2700\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by 2, we have:\n\n\\[\na + b = 5400\n\\]\n\nThe harmonic mean of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2ab}{a + b} = 75\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( a + b = 5400 \\) into the harmonic mean equation, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2ab}{5400} = 75\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by 5400, we have:\n\n\\[\n2ab = 75 \\times 5400\n\\]\n\nCalculating the right-hand side:\n\n\\[\n75 \\times 5400 = 405000\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n2ab = 405000\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 2, we find:\n\n\\[\nab = 202500\n\\]\n\nThe geometric mean of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{ab}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( ab = 202500 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{ab} = \\sqrt{202500}\n\\]\n\nTo find \\(\\sqrt{202500}\\), we can simplify:\n\n\\[\n202500 = 2025 \\times 100\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{202500} = \\sqrt{2025 \\times 100} = \\sqrt{2025} \\times \\sqrt{100} = \\sqrt{2025} \\times 10\n\\]\n\nNow, we find \\(\\sqrt{2025}\\). Notice that:\n\n\\[\n2025 = 45^2\n\\]\n\nTherefore:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{2025} = 45\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{202500} = 45 \\times 10 = 450\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the geometric mean of the two numbers is \\(\\boxed{450}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the sum \\(\\sum_{j = 1}^{2004} i^{2004 - F_j}\\), where \\(i\\) is the imaginary unit and \\(F_j\\) are the Fibonacci numbers.\n\nFirst, recall that the powers of \\(i\\) cycle every four terms:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\ni^1 &= i, \\\\\ni^2 &= -1, \\\\\ni^3 &= -i, \\\\\ni^4 &= 1, \\\\\ni^5 &= i, \\quad \\text{and so on.}\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(i^n\\) depends on \\(n \\mod 4\\).\n\nNext, we need to determine \\(2004 - F_j \\mod 4\\) for each Fibonacci number \\(F_j\\).\n\nThe Fibonacci sequence modulo 4 is periodic with a period of 6:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\nF_1 &\\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_2 &\\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_3 &\\equiv 2 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_4 &\\equiv 3 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_5 &\\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_6 &\\equiv 0 \\pmod{4}, \\\\\nF_7 &\\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}, \\quad \\text{and so on.}\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(2004 \\mod 4\\):\n\\[\n2004 \\equiv 0 \\pmod{4}.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(2004 - F_j \\equiv -F_j \\pmod{4}\\).\n\nUsing the periodicity of the Fibonacci sequence modulo 4, we find:\n- For \\(F_j \\equiv 0 \\pmod{4}\\), \\(2004 - F_j \\equiv 0 \\pmod{4}\\), so \\(i^{2004 - F_j} = i^0 = 1\\).\n- For \\(F_j \\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}\\), \\(2004 - F_j \\equiv -1 \\equiv 3 \\pmod{4}\\), so \\(i^{2004 - F_j} = i^3 = -i\\).\n- For \\(F_j \\equiv 2 \\pmod{4}\\), \\(2004 - F_j \\equiv -2 \\equiv 2 \\pmod{4}\\), so \\(i^{2004 - F_j} = i^2 = -1\\).\n- For \\(F_j \\equiv 3 \\pmod{4}\\), \\(2004 - F_j \\equiv -3 \\equiv 1 \\pmod{4}\\), so \\(i^{2004 - F_j} = i^1 = i\\).\n\nNow, count the occurrences of each residue class in the first 2004 Fibonacci numbers. Since the period is 6, each residue class appears equally often in each complete cycle of 6 terms. There are \\(\\left\\lfloor \\frac{2004}{6} \\right\\rfloor = 334\\) complete cycles, and each residue class appears 334 times in these cycles.\n\nThus, the sum is:\n\\[\n334 \\times (1 + (-i) + (-1) + i) = 334 \\times 0 = 0.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum \\(\\sum_{j = 1}^{2004} i^{2004 - F_j}\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the largest positive real number \\(\\lambda\\) such that for any nonnegative real numbers \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) satisfying \\(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 1\\), the inequality\n\n\\[\n\\lambda xy + yz \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nholds.\n\nFirst, let's consider the case where \\(z = 0\\). Then the condition becomes \\(x^2 + y^2 = 1\\), and the inequality simplifies to\n\n\\[\n\\lambda xy \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nUsing the AM-GM inequality, we have\n\n\\[\nxy \\le \\frac{x^2 + y^2}{2} = \\frac{1}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, we need\n\n\\[\n\\lambda \\cdot \\frac{1}{2} \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2},\n\\]\n\nwhich gives\n\n\\[\n\\lambda \\le \\sqrt{5}.\n\\]\n\nNext, consider the case where \\(x = y = z = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\). Then\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 3 \\left(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\right)^2 = 1,\n\\]\n\nand the inequality becomes\n\n\\[\n\\lambda \\left(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\right)^2 + \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}} \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\lambda}{3} + \\frac{1}{3} \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nMultiplying through by 3 gives\n\n\\[\n\\lambda + 1 \\le \\frac{3\\sqrt{5}}{2},\n\\]\n\nso\n\n\\[\n\\lambda \\le \\frac{3\\sqrt{5}}{2} - 1.\n\\]\n\nTo find the largest \\(\\lambda\\), we need to check if \\(\\lambda = \\sqrt{5}\\) satisfies the original inequality for all nonnegative \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) with \\(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 1\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(\\lambda = \\sqrt{5}\\) into the inequality, we have\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{5}xy + yz \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nFor \\(z = 0\\), this becomes\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{5}xy \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2},\n\\]\n\nwhich holds as shown earlier. For \\(x = y = z = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\), we have\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{5} \\cdot \\frac{1}{3} + \\frac{1}{3} \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2},\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{5} + 1}{3} \\le \\frac{\\sqrt{5}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nMultiplying through by 6 gives\n\n\\[\n2\\sqrt{5} + 2 \\le 3\\sqrt{5},\n\\]\n\nor\n\n\\[\n2 \\le \\sqrt{5},\n\n\\]\n\nwhich is true. Therefore, \\(\\lambda = \\sqrt{5}\\) satisfies the inequality for all nonnegative \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) with \\(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 1\\).\n\nThus, the largest positive real number \\(\\lambda\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{5}}\\)."
'To find the sum of the series \n\n\\[\n0.1 + 0.02 + 0.003 + 0.0004 + \\dots + \\frac{n}{10^n} + \\dotsb,\n\\]\n\nwe first express the general term of the series. 'To solve the equation \n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\left(\\frac{x}{x+1}\\right)^2 + 11}{\\left(\\frac{x}{x+1}\\right)^2 + 1} = 2,\n\\]\n\nlet \\( y = \\left(\\frac{x}{x+1}\\right)^2 \\). The equation becomes\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y + 11}{y + 1} = 2.\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives\n\n\\[\ny + 11 = 2(y + 1).\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side, we have\n\n\\[\ny + 11 = 2y + 2.\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we get\n\n\\[\n11 - 2 = 2y - y,\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to\n\n\\[\n9 = y.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( y = \\left(\\frac{x}{x+1}\\right)^2 \\), we have\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{x}{x+1}\\right)^2 = 9.\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we get\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x}{x+1} = 3 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad \\frac{x}{x+1} = -3.\n\\]\n\n**Case 1:** \\(\\frac{x}{x+1} = 3\\)\n\nSolving for \\( x \\), we have\n\n\\[\nx = 3(x + 1).\n\\]\n\nExpanding and rearranging terms, we get\n\n\\[\nx = 3x + 3 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 3 = 2x \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = \\frac{3}{2}.\n\\]\n\n**Case 2:** \\(\\frac{x}{x+1} = -3\\)\n\nSolving for \\( x \\), we have\n\n\\[\nx = -3(x + 1).\n\\]\n\nExpanding and rearranging terms, we get\n\n\\[\nx = -3x - 3 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 3x = -3 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = -1.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions to the equation are \\( x = \\frac{3}{2} \\) and \\( x = -1 \\).\n\nThe solutions are \\(\\boxed{\\frac{3}{2}, -1}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the remainder when the polynomial \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( (x - 3)(x - 1)^2 \\). According to the Remainder Theorem and the given conditions, we have:\n\n1. When \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( x - 3 \\), the remainder is 15. This means:\n   \\[\n   f(3) = 15.\n   \\]\n\n2. When \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( (x - 1)^2 \\), the remainder is \\( 2x + 1 \\). This implies:\n   \\[\n   f(x) = (x - 1)^2 q(x) + 2x + 1\n   \\]\n   for some polynomial \\( q(x) \\).\n\nWe are tasked with finding the remainder when \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( (x - 3)(x - 1)^2 \\). The remainder will be of the form:\n\\[\nR(x) = A(x - 1)^2 + B(x - 3) + C\n\\]\nwhere \\( A \\), \\( B \\), and \\( C \\) are constants. However, since the degree of the remainder must be less than the degree of the divisor, which is 3, the remainder can be expressed as:\n\\[\nR(x) = ax + b.\n\\]\n\nGiven the conditions, we have:\n- \\( f(3) = 15 \\), so substituting \\( x = 3 \\) into the remainder form gives:\n  \\[\n  3a + b = 15.\n  \\]\n\n- Since the remainder when divided by \\( (x - 1)^2 \\) is \\( 2x + 1 \\), we have:\n  \\[\n  f(1) = 2(1) + 1 = 3.\n  \\]\n  Substituting \\( x = 1 \\) into the remainder form gives:\n  \\[\n  a(1) + b = 3.\n  \\]\n\nNow, we solve the system of equations:\n1. \\( 3a + b = 15 \\)\n2. \\( a + b = 3 \\)\n\nSubtract the second equation from the first:\n\\[\n(3a + b) - (a + b) = 15 - 3\n\\]\n\\[\n2a = 12\n\\]\n\\[\na = 6\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( a = 6 \\) back into the second equation:\n\\[\n6 + b = 3\n\\]\n\\[\nb = 3 - 6 = -3\n\\]\n\nThus, the remainder when \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( (x - 3)(x - 1)^2 \\) is:\n\\[\nR(x) = 6x - 3.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the remainder is \\(\\boxed{6x - 3}\\).'
'To find the remainder when a polynomial \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\((x-1)(x-2)\\), we can use the Remainder Theorem. The remainder will be a linear polynomial of the form \\( ax + b \\).\n\nGiven that \\( f(1) = 2 \\) and \\( f(2) = 3 \\), we can express \\( f(x) \\) as:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = (x-1)(x-2)q(x) + ax + b\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( q(x) \\) is the quotient polynomial. \n\nSubstituting \\( x = 1 \\) into the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(1) = a(1) + b = 2\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[\na + b = 2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( x = 2 \\) into the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(2) = a(2) + b = 3\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2a + b = 3\n\\]\n\nWe now have a system of linear equations:\n\n1. \\( a + b = 2 \\)\n2. \\( 2a + b = 3 \\)\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(2a + b) - (a + b) = 3 - 2\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\na = 1\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( a = 1 \\) back into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n1 + b = 2\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( b \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nb = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the remainder when \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\((x-1)(x-2)\\) is:\n\n\\[\nax + b = 1x + 1 = x + 1\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the remainder is \\(\\boxed{x + 1}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \n\n\\[\n\\left| \\frac{3(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2x + 3} \\right| \\ge 1,\n\\]\n\nwe need to consider two cases: \n\n1. \\(\\frac{3(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2x + 3} \\ge 1\\)\n2. \\(\\frac{3(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2x + 3} \\le -1\\).\n\n### Case 1: \\(\\frac{3(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2x + 3} \\ge 1\\)\n\nThis inequality can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n3(x + 1) \\ge x^2 + 2x + 3.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n3x + 3 \\ge x^2 + 2x + 3.\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(x^2 + 2x + 3\\) from both sides gives:\n\n\\[\n3x + 3 - x^2 - 2x - 3 \\ge 0,\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n-x^2 + x \\ge 0.\n\\]\n\nFactoring, we get:\n\n\\[\n-x(x - 1) \\ge 0.\n\\]\n\nThis inequality holds when \\(x \\le 0\\) or \\(x \\ge 1\\).\n\n### Case 2: \\(\\frac{3(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2x + 3} \\le -1\\)\n\nThis inequality can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n3(x + 1) \\le -(x^2 + 2x + 3).\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n3x + 3 \\le -x^2 - 2x - 3.\n\\]\n\nAdding \\(x^2 + 2x + 3\\) to both sides gives:\n\n\\[\n3x + 3 + x^2 + 2x + 3 \\le 0,\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 5x + 6 \\le 0.\n\\]\n\nFactoring, we get:\n\n\\[\n(x + 2)(x + 3) \\le 0.\n\\]\n\nThis inequality holds when \\(-3 \\le x \\le -2\\).\n\n### Combining the Results\n\nThe solution to the original inequality is the union of the solutions from both cases:\n\n- From Case 1: \\(x \\le 0\\) or \\(x \\ge 1\\).\n- From Case 2: \\(-3 \\le x \\le -2\\).\n\nThus, the solution is:\n\n\\[\nx \\in [-3, -2] \\cup [1, \\infty).\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution set is \\(\\boxed{[-3, -2] \\cup [1, \\infty)}\\).'

"To solve for \\( f(5) \\), we start by analyzing the given functional equation:\n\n\\[\nf(x)f(2x^2) = f(2x^3 + x).\n\\]\n\nWe are also given that \\( f(0) = 1 \\) and \\( f(2) + f(3) = 125 \\).\n\nFirst, let's substitute \\( x = 0 \\) into the functional equation:\n\n\\[\nf(0)f(0) = f(0) \\implies 1 \\cdot 1 = 1,\n\\]\n\nwhich is consistent with \\( f(0) = 1 \\).\n\nNext, substitute \\( x = 1 \\):\n\n\\[\nf(1)f(2) = f(3).\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 2 \\):\n\n\\[\nf(2)f(8) = f(17).\n\\]\n\nWe also know:\n\n\\[\nf(2) + f(3) = 125.\n\\]\n\nFrom \\( f(1)f(2) = f(3) \\), we can express \\( f(3) \\) in terms of \\( f(1) \\) and \\( f(2) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(3) = f(1)f(2).\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this into the equation \\( f(2) + f(3) = 125 \\):\n\n\\[\nf(2) + f(1)f(2) = 125.\n\\]\n\nFactor out \\( f(2) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(2)(1 + f(1)) = 125.\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(2) = \\frac{125}{1 + f(1)}.\n\\]\n\nAssume \\( f(x) = x^3 + 1 \\). 'To solve this problem, we first need to determine the equations of the hyperbola \\(\\mathcal{H}\\) and the circle \\(\\mathcal{C}\\).\n\n### Equation of the Hyperbola\n\nThe hyperbola \\(\\mathcal{H}\\) has foci at \\((\\pm 5, 0)\\) and vertices at \\((\\pm 3, 0)\\). The standard form of a hyperbola centered at the origin with a horizontal transverse axis is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2}{a^2} - \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a\\) is the distance from the center to each vertex, and \\(c\\) is the distance from the center to each focus. We have \\(a = 3\\) and \\(c = 5\\).\n\nThe relationship between \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) for a hyperbola is given by:\n\n\\[\nc^2 = a^2 + b^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\n5^2 = 3^2 + b^2 \\implies 25 = 9 + b^2 \\implies b^2 = 16 \\implies b = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation of the hyperbola is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2}{9} - \\frac{y^2}{16} = 1\n\\]\n\n### Equation of the Circle\n\nThe circle \\(\\mathcal{C}\\) is centered at \\((0, 0)\\) with radius 4. Its equation is:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = 16\n\\]\n\n### Finding the Points of Intersection\n\nTo find the points of intersection, we solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\(\\frac{x^2}{9} - \\frac{y^2}{16} = 1\\)\n2. \\(x^2 + y^2 = 16\\)\n\nFrom the second equation, express \\(x^2\\) in terms of \\(y^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 16 - y^2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(x^2 = 16 - y^2\\) into the hyperbola equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{16 - y^2}{9} - \\frac{y^2}{16} = 1\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 144 (the least common multiple of 9 and 16) to clear the denominators:\n\n\\[\n16(16 - y^2) - 9y^2 = 144\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n256 - 16y^2 - 9y^2 = 144\n\\]\n\n\\[\n256 - 25y^2 = 144\n\\]\n\n\\[\n25y^2 = 112\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny^2 = \\frac{112}{25}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\pm \\frac{\\sqrt{112}}{5} = \\pm \\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back to find \\(x^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 16 - \\left(\\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5}\\right)^2 = 16 - \\frac{112}{25} = \\frac{400}{25} - \\frac{112}{25} = \\frac{288}{25}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\pm \\frac{\\sqrt{288}}{5} = \\pm \\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5}\n\\]\n\n### Coordinates of Intersection Points\n\nThe points of intersection are:\n\n\\[\n\\left( \\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5}, \\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5} \\right), \\left( \\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5}, -\\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5} \\right), \\left( -\\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5}, \\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5} \\right), \\left( -\\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5}, -\\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5} \\right)\n\\]\n\n### Area of the Quadrilateral\n\nThe quadrilateral is symmetric about both axes, forming a rectangle. The length of the sides parallel to the x-axis is:\n\n\\[\n2 \\times \\frac{12\\sqrt{2}}{5} = \\frac{24\\sqrt{2}}{5}\n\\]\n\nThe length of the sides parallel to the y-axis is:\n\n\\[\n2 \\times \\frac{4\\sqrt{7}}{5} = \\frac{8\\sqrt{7}}{5}\n\\]\n\nThe area of the rectangle is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{24\\sqrt{2}}{5}'
'To find the area of the circle that passes through all the intersection points of the given conics, we first need to determine the intersection points of the two equations:\n\n1. \\(4x^2 + 11y^2 = 29\\)\n2. \\(x^2 - 6y^2 = 6\\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. Start by solving the second equation for \\(x^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 6 + 6y^2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\(x^2\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n4(6 + 6y^2) + 11y^2 = 29\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n24 + 24y^2 + 11y^2 = 29\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n35y^2 + 24 = 29\n\\]\n\nSubtract 24 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n35y^2 = 5\n\\]\n\nDivide by 35:\n\n\\[\ny^2 = \\frac{1}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(y = \\pm \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\).\n\nNow, substitute \\(y^2 = \\frac{1}{7}\\) back into the expression for \\(x^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 6 + 6\\left(\\frac{1}{7}\\right) = 6 + \\frac{6}{7} = \\frac{42}{7} + \\frac{6}{7} = \\frac{48}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(x = \\pm \\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}\\).\n\nThe intersection points are \\(\\left(\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\), \\(\\left(-\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\), \\(\\left(\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\), and \\(\\left(-\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\).\n\nThese points are symmetric about both axes, indicating that they form a rectangle centered at the origin. The circle that passes through all these points is the circumcircle of this rectangle.\n\nThe distance between the points \\(\\left(\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\) and \\(\\left(-\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\) is the length of the rectangle, which is:\n\n\\[\n2\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}\n\\]\n\nThe distance between the points \\(\\left(\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\) and \\(\\left(\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}, -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)\\) is the width of the rectangle, which is:\n\n\\[\n2\\left(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right) = \\frac{2}{\\sqrt{7}}\n\\]\n\nThe diameter of the circumcircle is the diagonal of the rectangle, calculated using the Pythagorean theorem:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{\\left(2\\sqrt{\\frac{48}{7}}\\right)^2 + \\left(\\frac{2}{\\sqrt{7}}\\right)^2} = \\sqrt{\\frac{192}{7} + \\frac{4}{7}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{196}{7}} = \\sqrt{28} = 2\\sqrt{7}\n\\]\n\nThe radius \\(r\\) of the circle is half the diameter:\n\n\\[\nr = \\sqrt{7}\n\\]\n\nThe area of the circle is:\n\n\\[\n\\pi r^2 = \\pi (\\sqrt{7})^2 = 7\\pi\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the circle is \\(\\boxed{7\\pi}\\).'
'To find the largest \\( x \\) which is not in the domain of \\( g(x) = f(f(x)) \\), we first need to determine the domain of \\( f(x) = \\frac{1}{2x - 5} \\).\n\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) is undefined when the denominator is zero, i.e., when \\( 2x - 5 = 0 \\). Solving for \\( x \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n2x - 5 = 0 \\implies 2x = 5 \\implies x = \\frac{5}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( f(x) \\) is undefined at \\( x = \\frac{5}{2} \\).\n\nNext, we need to find when \\( f(f(x)) \\) is undefined. We have:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\frac{1}{2x - 5}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( f(x) \\) into itself, we get:\n\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = f\\left(\\frac{1}{2x - 5}\\right) = \\frac{1}{2\\left(\\frac{1}{2x - 5}\\right) - 5}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression inside the denominator:\n\n\\[\n2\\left(\\frac{1}{2x - 5}\\right) = \\frac{2}{2x - 5}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression for \\( f(f(x)) \\) becomes:\n\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = \\frac{1}{\\frac{2}{2x - 5} - 5}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{2x - 5} - 5 = \\frac{2 - 5(2x - 5)}{2x - 5} = \\frac{2 - (10x - 25)}{2x - 5} = \\frac{2 - 10x + 25}{2x - 5} = \\frac{27 - 10x}{2x - 5}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( f(f(x)) \\) is undefined when:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{27 - 10x}{2x - 5} = 0\n\\]\n\nThis occurs when the numerator is zero:\n\n\\[\n27 - 10x = 0 \\implies 10x = 27 \\implies x = \\frac{27}{10}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\( f(f(x)) \\) is undefined at \\( x = \\frac{27}{10} \\).\n\nAdditionally, \\( f(f(x)) \\) is undefined when the denominator of the inner function \\( f(x) \\) is zero, which we already found to be \\( x = \\frac{5}{2} \\).\n\nComparing \\( x = \\frac{5}{2} \\) and \\( x = \\frac{27}{10} \\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{5}{2} = 2.5 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\frac{27}{10} = 2.7\n\\]\n\nThe largest \\( x \\) which is not in the domain of \\( g(x) = f(f(x)) \\) is \\( \\boxed{\\frac{5}{2}} \\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to ensure that the polynomial \\( f(x) = x^4 + ax^3 + 3x^2 + bx + 1 \\) is non-negative for all real numbers \\( x \\). This suggests that the polynomial might be a perfect square or can be expressed as a product of two quadratics with non-negative leading coefficients.\n\nLet's first consider the possibility that \\( f(x) \\) is a perfect square. If \\( f(x) = (x^2 + px + q)^2 \\), then expanding gives:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 + px + q)^2 = x^4 + 2px^3 + (p^2 + 2q)x^2 + 2pqx + q^2\n\\]\n\nComparing coefficients with \\( f(x) = x^4 + ax^3 + 3x^2 + bx + 1 \\), we have:\n\n1. \\( 2p = a \\)\n2. \\( p^2 + 2q = 3 \\)\n3. \\( 2pq = b \\)\n4. \\( q^2 = 1 \\)\n\nFrom \\( q^2 = 1 \\), we have \\( q = \\pm 1 \\).\n\n**Case 1: \\( q = 1 \\)**\n\n- From \\( q^2 = 1 \\), we have \\( q = 1 \\).\n- Then, \\( p^2 + 2 \\cdot 1 = 3 \\) gives \\( p^2 = 1 \\), so \\( p = \\pm 1 \\).\n\n**Subcase 1.1: \\( p = 1 \\)**\n\n- \\( 2p = a \\) gives \\( a = 2 \\).\n- \\( 2pq = b \\) gives \\( b = 2 \\).\n\nThus, \\( a^2 + b^2 = 2^2 + 2^2 = 4 + 4 = 8 \\).\n\n**Subcase 1.2: \\( p = -1 \\)**\n\n- \\( 2p = a \\) gives \\( a = -2 \\).\n- \\( 2pq = b \\) gives \\( b = -2 \\).\n\nThus, \\( a^2 + b^2 = (-2)^2 + (-2)^2 = 4 + 4 = 8 \\).\n\n**Case 2: \\( q = -1 \\)**\n\n- From \\( q^2 = 1 \\), we have \\( q = -1 \\).\n- Then, \\( p^2 + 2(-1) = 3 \\) gives \\( p^2 = 5 \\), so \\( p = \\pm \\sqrt{5} \\).\n\n**Subcase 2.1: \\( p = \\sqrt{5} \\)**\n\n- \\( 2p = a \\) gives \\( a = 2\\sqrt{5} \\).\n- \\( 2pq = b \\) gives \\( b = -2\\sqrt{5} \\).\n\nThus, \\( a^2 + b^2 = (2\\sqrt{5})^2 + (-2\\sqrt{5})^2 = 20 + 20 = 40 \\).\n\n**Subcase 2.2: \\( p = -\\sqrt{5} \\)**\n\n- \\( 2p = a \\) gives \\( a = -2\\sqrt{5} \\).\n- \\( 2pq = b \\) gives \\( b = 2\\sqrt{5} \\).\n\nThus, \\( a^2 + b^2 = (-2\\sqrt{5})^2 + (2\\sqrt{5})^2 = 20 + 20 = 40 \\).\n\nThe largest possible value of \\( a^2 + b^2 \\) is therefore \\(\\boxed{40}\\)."
'To find a monic quadratic polynomial \\( P(x) \\) with integer coefficients such that \\( P(\\sqrt{13} - 3) = 0 \\), we start by letting \\( x = \\sqrt{13} - 3 \\). We need to express \\( \\sqrt{13} \\) in terms of \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx + 3 = \\sqrt{13}\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x + 3)^2 = 13\n\\]\n\nExpanding the left side, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 6x + 9 = 13\n\\]\n\nSubtracting 13 from both sides, we obtain:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 6x + 9 - 13 = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we find:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 6x - 4 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, the monic quadratic polynomial \\( P(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[\nP(x) = x^2 + 6x - 4\n\\]\n\nThis polynomial has integer coefficients and satisfies \\( P(\\sqrt{13} - 3) = 0 \\). Therefore, the answer is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{x^2 + 6x - 4}\n\\]'
'To solve for \\(\\left( \\frac{r}{s} \\right)^3\\), we start by analyzing the given equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r+s} = \\frac{1}{r} + \\frac{1}{s}.\n\\]\n\nFirst, we find a common denominator for the right-hand side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r} + \\frac{1}{s} = \\frac{s}{rs} + \\frac{r}{rs} = \\frac{r+s}{rs}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r+s} = \\frac{r+s}{rs}.\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\nrs = (r+s)^2.\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right-hand side, we have:\n\n\\[\nrs = r^2 + 2rs + s^2.\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we get:\n\n\\[\n0 = r^2 + 2rs + s^2 - rs = r^2 + rs + s^2.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\nr^2 + rs + s^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nTo find \\(\\left( \\frac{r}{s} \\right)^3\\), let \\(x = \\frac{r}{s}\\). Then \\(r = xs\\), and substituting into the equation gives:\n\n\\[\n(xs)^2 + xs \\cdot s + s^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^2s^2 + xs^2 + s^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nDividing the entire equation by \\(s^2\\) (since \\(s \\neq 0\\)), we obtain:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x + 1 = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe need to find \\(x^3\\). From the equation \\(x^2 + x + 1 = 0\\), we can express \\(x^3\\) in terms of \\(x\\):\n\nMultiply the equation by \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 + x^2 + x = 0.\n\\]\n\nUsing \\(x^2 = -x - 1\\) from the original equation, substitute for \\(x^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 + (-x - 1) + x = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - 1 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(x^3 = 1\\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\left( \\frac{r}{s} \\right)^3\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To find the product of the roots \\(abc\\) of the polynomial \\(x^3 - 3x - 5 = 0\\), we can use Vieta's formulas. For a cubic polynomial of the form \\(x^3 + px^2 + qx + r = 0\\), Vieta's formulas tell us that:\n\n- The sum of the roots \\(a + b + c = -p\\).\n- The sum of the products of the roots taken two at a time \\(ab + bc + ca = q\\).\n- The product of the roots \\(abc = -r\\).\n\nIn our polynomial \\(x^3 - 3x - 5 = 0\\), we can identify the coefficients as follows:\n\n- The coefficient of \\(x^2\\) is 0, so \\(p = 0\\).\n- The coefficient of \\(x\\) is \\(-3\\), so \\(q = -3\\).\n- The constant term is \\(-5\\), so \\(r = -5\\).\n\nUsing Vieta's formulas, the product of the roots \\(abc\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nabc = -r = -(-5) = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the roots \\(abc\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
'To find the coefficient of \\(x^{50}\\) in the given expression:\n\n\\[\n(1 + x)^{1000} + 2x (1 + x)^{999} + 3x^2 (1 + x)^{998} + \\dots + 1001x^{1000}\n\\]\n\nwe can express it as a sum:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{1000} (k+1) x^k (1+x)^{1000-k}\n\\]\n\nWe are interested in the coefficient of \\(x^{50}\\). This coefficient is obtained by considering terms where the power of \\(x\\) in \\(x^k (1+x)^{1000-k}\\) contributes to \\(x^{50}\\). Specifically, we need:\n\n\\[\nk + j = 50\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(j\\) is the power of \\(x\\) in the expansion of \\((1+x)^{1000-k}\\). Thus, \\(j = 50 - k\\).\n\nThe term \\((1+x)^{1000-k}\\) contributes \\(\\binom{1000-k}{50-k}\\) to the coefficient of \\(x^{50-k}\\). Therefore, the coefficient of \\(x^{50}\\) in the entire expression is:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} (k+1) \\binom{1000-k}{50-k}\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} (k+1) \\binom{1000-k}{950}\n\\]\n\nTo simplify this, we use the Hockey Stick Identity (or Christmas Stocking Theorem), which states:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{i=r}^{n} \\binom{i}{r} = \\binom{n+1}{r+1}\n\\]\n\nApplying this identity, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} \\binom{1000-k}{950} = \\binom{1001}{951}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to evaluate:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} k \\binom{1000-k}{950}\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten using the identity:\n\n\\[\nk \\binom{1000-k}{950} = (1000-k) \\binom{999-k}{949}\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} k \\binom{1000-k}{950} = \\sum_{k=0}^{50} (1000-k) \\binom{999-k}{949}\n\\]\n\nThis sum can be evaluated using the Hockey Stick Identity again:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} \\binom{999-k}{949} = \\binom{1000}{950}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the coefficient of \\(x^{50}\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=0}^{50} (k+1) \\binom{1000-k}{950} = \\binom{1001}{951} + \\binom{1000}{950}\n\\]\n\nThe smallest possible value of \\(n+k\\) for \\(\\binom{n}{k}\\) is when \\(n = 1001\\) and \\(k = 951\\), giving:\n\n\\[\nn + k = 1001 + 951 = 1952\n\\]\n\nThus, the smallest possible value of \\(n+k\\) is \\(\\boxed{1952}\\).'
'To find the largest possible area of a rectangle inscribed in a unit circle, we can use the fact that the rectangle with the maximum area that can be inscribed in a circle is a square.\n\nConsider a rectangle inscribed in a unit circle. The diagonal of the rectangle is the diameter of the circle, which is 2 (since the radius of the unit circle is 1). Let the sides of the rectangle be \\(a\\) and \\(b\\). By the Pythagorean theorem, we have:\n\n\\[\na^2 + b^2 = 2^2 = 4.\n\\]\n\nThe area \\(A\\) of the rectangle is given by:\n\n\\[\nA = a \\times b.\n\\]\n\nTo maximize the area, we can use the AM-GM inequality, which states that for non-negative numbers \\(a\\) and \\(b\\),\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a^2 + b^2}{2} \\geq \\sqrt{a^2 \\cdot b^2}.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(a^2 + b^2 = 4\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{4}{2} \\geq \\sqrt{a^2 \\cdot b^2},\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2 \\geq \\sqrt{a^2 \\cdot b^2}.\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we get:\n\n\\[\n4 \\geq a^2 \\cdot b^2.\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\n2 \\geq a \\cdot b.\n\\]\n\nThe equality holds when \\(a = b\\), meaning the rectangle is a square. Therefore, the maximum area occurs when the rectangle is a square with side length \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\), since:\n\n\\[\na^2 + a^2 = 4 \\implies 2a^2 = 4 \\implies a^2 = 2 \\implies a = \\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the maximum area of the rectangle is:\n\n\\[\nA = a \\times a = \\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) \\times \\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) = \\frac{2}{2} = 1.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the largest possible area of the rectangle is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the largest value of \\( k \\) such that both \\( Q_1(x) = x^2 + (k - 29)x - k \\) and \\( Q_2(x) = 2x^2 + (2k - 43)x + k \\) are factors of a cubic polynomial \\( P(x) \\).\n\nSince \\( P(x) \\) is a cubic polynomial, it can be expressed as the product of a linear polynomial and one of the given quadratic polynomials.
