'To find the integer roots of the polynomial \\(x^4 + 5x^3 + 9x^2 - x - 14 = 0\\), we can use the Rational Root Theorem. This theorem states that any rational root, in the form of \\(\\frac{p}{q}\\), must have \\(p\\) as a factor of the constant term and \\(q\\) as a factor of the leading coefficient.\n\nIn this polynomial, the constant term is \\(-14\\) and the leading coefficient is \\(1\\). Therefore, the possible integer roots are the factors of \\(-14\\), which are \\(\\pm 1, \\pm 2, \\pm 7, \\pm 14\\).\n\nWe will test these possible roots by substituting them into the polynomial:\n\n1. \\(x = 1\\):\n   \\[\n   1^4 + 5 \\cdot 1^3 + 9 \\cdot 1^2 - 1 - 14 = 1 + 5 + 9 - 1 - 14 = 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = 1\\) is a root.\n\n2. \\(x = -1\\):\n   \\[\n   (-1)^4 + 5 \\cdot (-1)^3 + 9 \\cdot (-1)^2 - (-1) - 14 = 1 - 5 + 9 + 1 - 14 = -8\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = -1\\) is not a root.\n\n3. \\(x = 2\\):\n   \\[\n   2^4 + 5 \\cdot 2^3 + 9 \\cdot 2^2 - 2 - 14 = 16 + 40 + 36 - 2 - 14 = 76\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = 2\\) is not a root.\n\n4. \\(x = -2\\):\n   \\[\n   (-2)^4 + 5 \\cdot (-2)^3 + 9 \\cdot (-2)^2 - (-2) - 14 = 16 - 40 + 36 + 2 - 14 = 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = -2\\) is a root.\n\n5. \\(x = 7\\):\n   \\[\n   7^4 + 5 \\cdot 7^3 + 9 \\cdot 7^2 - 7 - 14 = 2401 + 1715 + 441 - 7 - 14 = 4536\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = 7\\) is not a root.\n\n6. \\(x = -7\\):\n   \\[\n   (-7)^4 + 5 \\cdot (-7)^3 + 9 \\cdot (-7)^2 - (-7) - 14 = 2401 - 1715 + 441 + 7 - 14 = 1120\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = -7\\) is not a root.\n\n7. \\(x = 14\\):\n   \\[\n   14^4 + 5 \\cdot 14^3 + 9 \\cdot 14^2 - 14 - 14 = 38416 + 13720 + 1764 - 14 - 14 = 53872\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = 14\\) is not a root.\n\n8. \\(x = -14\\):\n   \\[\n   (-14)^4 + 5 \\cdot (-14)^3 + 9 \\cdot (-14)^2 - (-14) - 14 = 38416 - 13720 + 1764 + 14 - 14 = 23044\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = -14\\) is not a root.\n\nThe integer roots of the polynomial are \\(x = 1\\) and \\(x = -2\\). Therefore, the integer roots are \\(\\boxed{1, -2}\\).'
'To solve for the greatest possible value of \\(\\frac{r^3-1}{r^5+r^4-r^3-r^2}\\) where \\(r\\) is a root of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 2x - 15 = 0\\), we first need to find the roots of the equation.\n\nThe quadratic equation is given by:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 2x - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can solve this using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 2\\), and \\(c = -15\\). Plugging in these values, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{2^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-15)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{4 + 60}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{64}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-2 \\pm 8}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us the roots:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{6}{2} = 3 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{-10}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nThus, the roots are \\(r = 3\\) and \\(r = -5\\).\n\nNext, we evaluate the expression \\(\\frac{r^3-1}{r^5+r^4-r^3-r^2}\\) for each root.\n\n**For \\(r = 3\\):**\n\nCalculate \\(r^3\\), \\(r^5\\), \\(r^4\\), and \\(r^2\\):\n\n\\[\nr^3 = 3^3 = 27, \\quad r^5 = 3^5 = 243, \\quad r^4 = 3^4 = 81, \\quad r^2 = 3^2 = 9\n\\]\n\nSubstitute these into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{r^3-1}{r^5+r^4-r^3-r^2} = \\frac{27 - 1}{243 + 81 - 27 - 9}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{26}{288}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{13}{144}\n\\]\n\n**For \\(r = -5\\):**\n\nCalculate \\(r^3\\), \\(r^5\\), \\(r^4\\), and \\(r^2\\):\n\n\\[\nr^3 = (-5)^3 = -125, \\quad r^5 = (-5)^5 = -3125, \\quad r^4 = (-5)^4 = 625, \\quad r^2 = (-5)^2 = 25\n\\]\n\nSubstitute these into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{r^3-1}{r^5+r^4-r^3-r^2} = \\frac{-125 - 1}{-3125 + 625 + 125 - 25}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{-126}{-2400}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{21}{400}\n\\]\n\nComparing the two values \\(\\frac{13}{144}\\) and \\(\\frac{21}{400}\\), we find the greatest value by comparing their decimal equivalents:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{13}{144} \\approx 0.0903, \\quad \\frac{21}{400} = 0.0525\n\\]\n\nThus, the greatest possible value is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{13}{144}}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we start by letting \\( x = \\frac{a}{b} \\), \\( y = \\frac{b}{c} \\), and \\( z = \\frac{c}{a} \\). This gives us the equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y + z = 7\n\\]\n\nand\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{y} + \\frac{1}{z} = 9.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x = \\frac{a}{b} \\), \\( y = \\frac{b}{c} \\), and \\( z = \\frac{c}{a} \\), it follows that \\( xyz = \\frac{a}{b} \\cdot \\frac{b}{c} \\cdot \\frac{c}{a} = 1 \\).\n\nWe need to find \\( x^3 + y^3 + z^3 \\).\n\nUsing the identity for the sum of cubes, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = (x + y + z)(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 - xy - yz - zx) + 3xyz.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( xyz = 1 \\), we can substitute this into the equation:\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = (x + y + z)(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 - xy - yz - zx) + 3.\n\\]\n\nWe also know:\n\n\\[\nx + y + z = 7\n\\]\n\nand\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{y} + \\frac{1}{z} = \\frac{xy + yz + zx}{xyz} = xy + yz + zx = 9.\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( x^2 + y^2 + z^2 \\). We use the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = (x + y + z)^2 - 2(xy + yz + zx).\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 7^2 - 2 \\times 9 = 49 - 18 = 31.\n\\]\n\nNow substitute back into the expression for \\( x^3 + y^3 + z^3 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 + y^3 + z^3 = 7(31 - 9) + 3 = 7 \\times 22 + 3 = 154 + 3 = 157.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( \\frac{a^3}{b^3} + \\frac{b^3}{c^3} + \\frac{c^3}{a^3} \\) is \\(\\boxed{157}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \n\n\\[\n\\dfrac{1}{x-2009}+\\dfrac{1}{x-2010}+\\dfrac{1}{x-2011}\\ge 1,\n\\]\n\nwe first find a common denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(x-2010)(x-2011) + (x-2009)(x-2011) + (x-2009)(x-2010)}{(x-2009)(x-2010)(x-2011)} \\ge 1.\n\\]\n\nThe numerator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(x-2010)(x-2011) + (x-2009)(x-2011) + (x-2009)(x-2010).\n\\]\n\nExpanding each term, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x-2010)(x-2011) = x^2 - 4021x + 2010 \\times 2011,\n\\]\n\\[\n(x-2009)(x-2011) = x^2 - 4020x + 2009 \\times 2011,\n\\]\n\\[\n(x-2009)(x-2010) = x^2 - 4019x + 2009 \\times 2010.\n\\]\n\nAdding these, the quadratic terms sum to:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 - (4021 + 4020 + 4019)x + (2010 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2010).\n\\]\n\nThe linear term simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 - 12060x.\n\\]\n\nThe constant term is:\n\n\\[\n2010 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2010.\n\\]\n\nWe need to solve:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 - 12060x + (2010 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2010) \\ge (x-2009)(x-2010)(x-2011).\n\\]\n\nThe right-hand side expands to:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - (2009 + 2010 + 2011)x^2 + (2009 \\times 2010 + 2010 \\times 2011 + 2011 \\times 2009)x - 2009 \\times 2010 \\times 2011.\n\\]\n\nThe inequality becomes:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 - 12060x + (2010 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2010) \\ge x^3 - 6029x^2 + (2009 \\times 2010 + 2010 \\times 2011 + 2011 \\times 2009)x - 2009 \\times 2010 \\times 2011.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we find:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - 6029x^2 + 3x^2 - 12060x + (2010 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2011 + 2009 \\times 2010) \\ge 0.\n\\]\n\nThis inequality is satisfied when \\(x\\) is outside the roots of the cubic equation. The roots are approximately 2009, 2010, and 2011. The intervals where the inequality holds are:\n\n\\[\n(-\\infty, 2009) \\cup (2009, 2010) \\cup (2010, 2011) \\cup (2011, \\infty).\n\\]\n\nThe lengths of the intervals are:\n\n\\[\n(2009 - (-\\infty)) + (2010 - 2009) + (2011 - 2010) + (\\infty - 2011).\n\\]\n\nThe finite intervals are:\n\n\\[\n1 + 1 = 2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of the lengths of these intervals is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To find the minimum value of the expression \\(\\left( a + \\frac{1}{a} \\right)^2 + \\left( b + \\frac{1}{b} \\right)^2\\) given that \\(a + b = 1\\), we start by expanding each term:\n\n\\[\n\\left( a + \\frac{1}{a} \\right)^2 = a^2 + 2 + \\frac{1}{a^2}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\left( b + \\frac{1}{b} \\right)^2 = b^2 + 2 + \\frac{1}{b^2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\na^2 + 2 + \\frac{1}{a^2} + b^2 + 2 + \\frac{1}{b^2} = a^2 + b^2 + \\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2} + 4\n\\]\n\nUsing the identity \\((a + b)^2 = a^2 + b^2 + 2ab\\), and knowing \\(a + b = 1\\), we have:\n\n\\[\na^2 + b^2 = (a + b)^2 - 2ab = 1 - 2ab\n\\]\n\nSubstituting this into our expression, we get:\n\n\\[\n1 - 2ab + \\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2} + 4\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to minimize:\n\n\\[\n1 - 2ab + \\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2} + 4 = 5 - 2ab + \\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2}\n\\]\n\nTo simplify \\(\\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2}\\), we use the AM-GM inequality:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{a^2} + \\frac{1}{b^2} \\geq \\frac{2}{ab}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n5 - 2ab + \\frac{2}{ab}\n\\]\n\nLet \\(x = ab\\). Then, we need to minimize:\n\n\\[\n5 - 2x + \\frac{2}{x}\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum, we take the derivative with respect to \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nf(x) = 5 - 2x + \\frac{2}{x}\n\\]\n\\[\nf'(x) = -2 - \\frac{2}{x^2}\n\\]\n\nSetting \\(f'(x) = 0\\), we solve:\n\n\\[\n-2 - \\frac{2}{x^2} = 0 \\implies \\frac{2}{x^2} = 2 \\implies x^2 = 1 \\implies x = 1\n\\]\n\nSince \\(x = ab\\) and \\(a + b = 1\\), the maximum value of \\(ab\\) is \\(\\frac{1}{4}\\) (by AM-GM inequality), not 1. Therefore, we need to check the boundary condition \\(x = \\frac{1}{4}\\):\n\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right) = 5 - 2\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right) + \\frac{2}{\\frac{1}{4}} = 5 - \\frac{1}{2} + 8 = 12.5\n\\]\n\nThus, the minimum value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{12.5}\\).\n\nJonathon's mistake was assuming that the minimum value of each squared term separately would lead to the minimum of the entire expression. However, the constraint \\(a + b = 1\\) affects the values of \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) such that the minimum of the entire expression is not simply the sum of the minimums of the individual terms."
'To find the equation of the line that is tangent to both parabolas \\( y^2 = 4x \\) and \\( x^2 = -32y \\), we start by considering the general form of a line \\( y = mx + b \\).\n\n### Tangency with \\( y^2 = 4x \\)\n\nFor the parabola \\( y^2 = 4x \\), the slope of the tangent line at a point \\((x_1, y_1)\\) on the parabola is given by differentiating implicitly:\n\n\\[\n2y \\frac{dy}{dx} = 4 \\implies \\frac{dy}{dx} = \\frac{2}{y}\n\\]\n\nThe slope of the tangent line is \\( m = \\frac{2}{y_1} \\). Since the point \\((x_1, y_1)\\) lies on the parabola, we have \\( y_1^2 = 4x_1 \\). The equation of the tangent line is:\n\n\\[\ny - y_1 = \\frac{2}{y_1}(x - x_1)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( x_1 = \\frac{y_1^2}{4} \\) into the equation, we get:\n\n\\[\ny - y_1 = \\frac{2}{y_1}\\left(x - \\frac{y_1^2}{4}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2}{y_1}x - \\frac{y_1}{2} + y_1\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2}{y_1}x + \\frac{y_1}{2}\n\\]\n\n### Tangency with \\( x^2 = -32y \\)\n\nFor the parabola \\( x^2 = -32y \\), the slope of the tangent line at a point \\((x_2, y_2)\\) on the parabola is given by differentiating implicitly:\n\n\\[\n2x \\frac{dx}{dy} = -32 \\implies \\frac{dx}{dy} = -\\frac{16}{x}\n\\]\n\nThe slope of the tangent line is \\( m = -\\frac{16}{x_2} \\). Since the point \\((x_2, y_2)\\) lies on the parabola, we have \\( x_2^2 = -32y_2 \\). The equation of the tangent line is:\n\n\\[\ny - y_2 = -\\frac{16}{x_2}(x - x_2)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( y_2 = -\\frac{x_2^2}{32} \\) into the equation, we get:\n\n\\[\ny + \\frac{x_2^2}{32} = -\\frac{16}{x_2}(x - x_2)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\ny = -\\frac{16}{x_2}x + 16 + \\frac{x_2^2}{32}\n\\]\n\n### Equating the Slopes\n\nFor the line to be tangent to both parabolas, the slopes must be equal:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{y_1} = -\\frac{16}{x_2}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\n2x_2 = -16y_1 \\implies x_2 = -8y_1\n\\]\n\n### Solving for the Line\n\nSubstitute \\( x_2 = -8y_1 \\) into the equation \\( x_2^2 = -32y_2 \\):\n\n\\[\n(-8y_1)^2 = -32y_2 \\implies 64y_1^2 = -32y_2 \\implies y_2 = -2y_1^2\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( y_1^2 = 4x_1 \\) into \\( y_2 = -2y_1^2 \\):\n\n\\[\ny_2 = -2(4x_1) = -8x_1\n\\]\n\nThe line equation \\( y = mx + b \\) becomes:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2}{y_1}x + \\frac{y_1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( y_1 = 2 \\) (from \\( y_1^2 = 4x_1 \\) and \\( x_1 = 1 \\)):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2}{2}x + \\frac{2}{2} = x + 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation of the line tangent to both parabolas is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{y = x + 1}\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\((ac+bd)^2 + (bc-ad)^2\\), we can use the identity for the sum of squares of two expressions:\n\n\\[\n(ac+bd)^2 + (bc-ad)^2 = (ac)^2 + (bd)^2 + 2(ac)(bd) + (bc)^2 + (ad)^2 - 2(bc)(ad).\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\na^2c^2 + b^2d^2 + 2abcd + b^2c^2 + a^2d^2 - 2abcd.\n\\]\n\nNotice that the terms \\(2abcd\\) and \\(-2abcd\\) cancel each other out, leaving us with:\n\n\\[\na^2c^2 + b^2d^2 + b^2c^2 + a^2d^2.\n\\]\n\nWe can rearrange and group the terms as follows:\n\n\\[\na^2c^2 + a^2d^2 + b^2c^2 + b^2d^2 = a^2(c^2 + d^2) + b^2(c^2 + d^2).\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\(c^2 + d^2 = 4\\), we substitute this into the expression:\n\n\\[\na^2 \\cdot 4 + b^2 \\cdot 4 = 4(a^2 + b^2).\n\\]\n\nSince we know \\(a^2 + b^2 = 3\\), we substitute this value:\n\n\\[\n4 \\times 3 = 12.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\((ac+bd)^2 + (bc-ad)^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we need to find the smallest positive integer \\( x \\) greater than 9 such that:\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor x \\rfloor - 19 \\left\\lfloor \\frac{x}{19} \\right\\rfloor = 9\n\\]\n\nand\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor x \\rfloor - 89 \\left\\lfloor \\frac{x}{89} \\right\\rfloor = 9.\n\\]\n\nLet's denote \\( \\lfloor x \\rfloor = n \\). Then the conditions become:\n\n1. \\( n - 19 \\left\\lfloor \\frac{n}{19} \\right\\rfloor = 9 \\)\n2. \\( n - 89 \\left\\lfloor \\frac{n}{89} \\right\\rfloor = 9 \\)\n\nThese equations imply:\n\n\\[\nn \\equiv 9 \\pmod{19}\n\\]\n\nand\n\n\\[\nn \\equiv 9 \\pmod{89}.\n\\]\n\nSince 19 and 89 are coprime, we can use the Chinese Remainder Theorem to find a unique solution modulo \\( 19 \\times 89 = 1691 \\).\n\nThe solution to the system of congruences is:\n\n\\[\nn \\equiv 9 \\pmod{1691}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the smallest positive integer \\( n \\) greater than 9 that satisfies both congruences is \\( n = 9 \\).\n\nHowever, since \\( x \\) must be greater than 9, we need to find the next solution:\n\n\\[\nn = 9 + 1691k\n\\]\n\nfor the smallest \\( k \\) such that \\( n > 9 \\). The smallest \\( k \\) is 1, so:\n\n\\[\nn = 9 + 1691 \\times 1 = 1700.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the smallest positive integer \\( x \\) greater than 9 that satisfies both conditions is \\( \\boxed{1700} \\)."
'To solve for \\( p(11) \\), we start by considering the polynomial \\( p(x) \\). Given that \\( p(-3) = 4 \\), \\( p(-2) = 4 \\), and \\( p(4) = 4 \\), we can infer that \\( p(x) - 4 \\) has roots at \\( x = -3, -2, \\) and \\( 4 \\). Therefore, we can express \\( p(x) \\) as:\n\n\\[\np(x) = a(x + 3)(x + 2)(x - 4) + 4\n\\]\n\nWe also know that \\( p(5) = 16 \\). Substituting \\( x = 5 \\) into the expression for \\( p(x) \\), we have:\n\n\\[\np(5) = a(5 + 3)(5 + 2)(5 - 4) + 4 = 16\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\na(8)(7)(1) + 4 = 16\n\\]\n\n\\[\n56a + 4 = 16\n\\]\n\n\\[\n56a = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{12}{56} = \\frac{3}{14}\n\\]\n\nNow, we have the polynomial:\n\n\\[\np(x) = \\frac{3}{14}(x + 3)(x + 2)(x - 4) + 4\n\\]\n\nWe need to find \\( p(11) \\). Substituting \\( x = 11 \\) into the polynomial, we have:\n\n\\[\np(11) = \\frac{3}{14}(11 + 3)(11 + 2)(11 - 4) + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{3}{14}(14)(13)(7) + 4\n\\]\n\nCalculating the product:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{3}{14} \\times 14 \\times 13 \\times 7 + 4\n\\]\n\nThe \\( 14 \\) in the numerator and denominator cancel out:\n\n\\[\n= 3 \\times 13 \\times 7 + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 3 \\times 91 + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 273 + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 277\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( p(11) \\) is \\(\\boxed{277}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the area of the region in the \\(xy\\)-plane where the product of the floor functions of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) equals 16. That is, we need to find the set of points \\((x, y)\\) such that:\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor x \\rfloor \\lfloor y \\rfloor = 16.\n\\]\n\nThe floor function \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) gives the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\). Therefore, for \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor \\lfloor y \\rfloor = 16\\), both \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) and \\(\\lfloor y \\rfloor\\) must be integers whose product is 16. The possible pairs \\((\\lfloor x \\rfloor, \\lfloor y \\rfloor)\\) are:\n\n\\[\n(1, 16), (2, 8), (4, 4), (8, 2), (16, 1), (-1, -16), (-2, -8), (-4, -4), (-8, -2), (-16, -1).\n\\]\n\nFor each pair \\((a, b)\\), the region in the \\(xy\\)-plane is defined by:\n\n\\[\na \\leq x < a+1 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b \\leq y < b+1.\n\\]\n\nThe area of each such region is \\(1 \\times 1 = 1\\).\n\nNow, we count the number of such regions. There are 10 pairs listed above, each corresponding to a distinct unit square in the \\(xy\\)-plane. Therefore, the total area of the region satisfying \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor \\lfloor y \\rfloor = 16\\) is:\n\n\\[\n10 \\times 1 = 10.\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the region is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"To solve for \\( f(x) \\), we start with the given functional equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 f(x) + f(1-x) = -x^4 + 2x\n\\]\n\nFirst, substitute \\( x = 1-x \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n(1-x)^2 f(1-x) + f(x) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x)\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two equations:\n\n1. \\( x^2 f(x) + f(1-x) = -x^4 + 2x \\)\n2. \\( (1-x)^2 f(1-x) + f(x) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x) \\)\n\nNow, solve these equations simultaneously. From equation 1, express \\( f(1-x) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(1-x) = -x^4 + 2x - x^2 f(x)\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this into equation 2:\n\n\\[\n(1-x)^2 (-x^4 + 2x - x^2 f(x)) + f(x) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x)\n\\]\n\nSimplify the left side:\n\n\\[\n-(1-x)^2 x^4 + 2x(1-x)^2 - x^2(1-x)^2 f(x) + f(x) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x)\n\\]\n\nCombine terms involving \\( f(x) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(x) (1 - x^2(1-x)^2) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x) + (1-x)^2 x^4 - 2x(1-x)^2\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\nf(x) (1 - x^2 + 2x^3 - x^4) = -(1-x)^4 + 2(1-x) + x^4(1-x)^2 - 2x(1-x)^2\n\\]\n\nThe expression for \\( f(x) \\) becomes complex, so let's try specific values to find \\( \\alpha \\) and \\( \\beta \\).\n\nSet \\( x = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\n0^2 f(0) + f(1) = 0 + 0 \\implies f(1) = 0\n\\]\n\nSet \\( x = 1 \\):\n\n\\[\n1^2 f(1) + f(0) = -1 + 2 \\implies f(0) = 1\n\\]\n\nNow, check for values where \\( x^2 = 1 \\) (i.e., \\( x = 1 \\) or \\( x = -1 \\)):\n\nFor \\( x = 1 \\), we already have \\( f(1) = 0 \\).\n\nFor \\( x = -1 \\):\n\n\\[\n(-1)^2 f(-1) + f(2) = -(-1)^4 + 2(-1) \\implies f(-1) + f(2) = -1 - 2 = -3\n\\]\n\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) is not determined for \\( x = -1 \\) and \\( x = 2 \\). Therefore, \\( \\alpha = -1 \\) and \\( \\beta = 2 \\).\n\nFinally, compute \\( \\alpha^2 + \\beta^2 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\alpha^2 + \\beta^2 = (-1)^2 + 2^2 = 1 + 4 = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
'Let \\( z = bi \\) where \\( b \\) is a real number. Since \\( z \\) is a root of the equation \\( z^2 + z + \\omega = 0 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(bi)^2 + bi + \\omega = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n-b^2 + bi + \\omega = 0\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\n\\omega = b^2 - bi\n\\]\n\nSince \\( |\\omega| = 1 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n|\\omega| = |b^2 - bi| = 1\n\\]\n\nThe magnitude of a complex number \\( a + bi \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{a^2 + b^2}\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{(b^2)^2 + (-b)^2} = 1\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{b^4 + b^2} = 1\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we obtain:\n\n\\[\nb^4 + b^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nLet \\( x = b^2 \\). Then the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 1 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4}}{2} = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x = b^2 \\) must be non-negative, we choose:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( b^2 = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\).\n\nNow, substituting back to find \\( \\omega \\):\n\n\\[\n\\omega = b^2 - bi = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} - bi\n\\]\n\nWe need to find \\( \\omega + \\overline{\\omega} \\). The conjugate of \\( \\omega \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\overline{\\omega} = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} + bi\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n\\omega + \\overline{\\omega} = \\left(\\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} - bi\\right) + \\left(\\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} + bi\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\omega + \\overline{\\omega} = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} + \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} = -1 + \\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( \\omega + \\overline{\\omega} \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\).'
'To find the sum of all complex numbers \\( z \\) that satisfy the equation\n\n\\[\nz^3 + z^2 - |z|^2 + 2z = 0,\n\\]\n\nwe start by expressing \\( |z|^2 \\) in terms of \\( z \\). If \\( z = a + bi \\), then \\( |z|^2 = a^2 + b^2 \\). However, we can also express \\( |z|^2 \\) as \\( z \\overline{z} \\), where \\( \\overline{z} \\) is the complex conjugate of \\( z \\).\n\nThe equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nz^3 + z^2 - z\\overline{z} + 2z = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe can factor out \\( z \\) from the equation:\n\n\\[\nz(z^2 + z + 2) - z\\overline{z} = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\nz(z^2 + z + 2 - \\overline{z}) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two cases to consider:\n\n1. \\( z = 0 \\).\n2. \\( z^2 + z + 2 - \\overline{z} = 0 \\).\n\nFor the first case, \\( z = 0 \\) is a solution.\n\nFor the second case, we have:\n\n\\[\nz^2 + z + 2 - \\overline{z} = 0.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( z = a + bi \\) and \\( \\overline{z} = a - bi \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n(a + bi)^2 + (a + bi) + 2 - (a - bi) = 0.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 - b^2 + 2abi) + (a + bi) + 2 - a + bi = 0.\n\\]\n\nCombining like terms, we get:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 - b^2 + 2abi + a + bi + 2 - a + bi) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 - b^2 + 2abi + bi + 2) = 0.\n\\]\n\nSeparating real and imaginary parts, we have:\n\nReal part: \\( a^2 - b^2 + 2 = 0 \\).\n\nImaginary part: \\( 2ab + 2b = 0 \\).\n\nFrom the imaginary part, we factor out \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nb(2a + 2) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis gives \\( b = 0 \\) or \\( a = -1 \\).\n\n**Case 1:** \\( b = 0 \\).\n\nThen the real part equation becomes:\n\n\\[\na^2 + 2 = 0,\n\\]\n\nwhich has no real solutions for \\( a \\).\n\n**Case 2:** \\( a = -1 \\).\n\nThen the real part equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(-1)^2 - b^2 + 2 = 0 \\Rightarrow 1 - b^2 + 2 = 0 \\Rightarrow 3 - b^2 = 0 \\Rightarrow b^2 = 3.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( b = \\sqrt{3} \\) or \\( b = -\\sqrt{3} \\).\n\nThe solutions for \\( z \\) are \\( z = -1 + \\sqrt{3}i \\) and \\( z = -1 - \\sqrt{3}i \\).\n\nNow, we sum all solutions:\n\n1. \\( z = 0 \\).\n2. \\( z = -1 + \\sqrt{3}i \\).\n3. \\( z = -1 - \\sqrt{3}i \\).\n\nThe sum is:\n\n\\[\n0 + (-1 + \\sqrt{3}i) + (-1 - \\sqrt{3}i) = -1 - 1 = -2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of all complex numbers \\( z \\) that satisfy the equation is \\(\\boxed{-2}\\).'
"To solve the functional equation \\( f(x) + f(y) = f(x+y) - xy - 1 \\), we first try to find a general form for \\( f(x) \\).\n\n### Step 1: Find \\( f(0) \\)\n\nSet \\( x = 0 \\) in the functional equation:\n\\[\nf(0) + f(y) = f(y) - 0 \\cdot y - 1 \\implies f(0) = -1.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Find \\( f(x) \\) for specific values\n\nSet \\( y = 1 \\) in the functional equation:\n\\[\nf(x) + f(1) = f(x+1) - x \\cdot 1 - 1.\n\\]\nGiven \\( f(1) = 1 \\), we have:\n\\[\nf(x) + 1 = f(x+1) - x - 1 \\implies f(x+1) = f(x) + x + 2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Find a pattern for \\( f(x) \\)\n\nUsing the recursive relation \\( f(x+1) = f(x) + x + 2 \\), we can compute:\n- \\( f(1) = 1 \\)\n- \\( f(2) = f(1) + 1 + 2 = 1 + 3 = 4 \\)\n- \\( f(3) = f(2) + 2 + 2 = 4 + 4 = 8 \\)\n- \\( f(4) = f(3) + 3 + 2 = 8 + 5 = 13 \\)\n\nWe observe that \\( f(n) \\) seems to follow a quadratic pattern. Let's assume \\( f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c \\) and determine \\( a, b, c \\).\n\n### Step 4: Determine the coefficients\n\nUsing the recursive relation:\n\\[\nf(x+1) = ax^2 + bx + c + x + 2 = a(x+1)^2 + b(x+1) + c.\n\\]\nExpanding the right side:\n\\[\na(x^2 + 2x + 1) + b(x + 1) + c = ax^2 + 2ax + a + bx + b + c.\n\\]\nEquating coefficients with \\( ax^2 + (b + 2a)x + (a + b + c) \\), we have:\n- \\( a = a \\)\n- \\( b + 2a = b + 1 \\) implies \\( 2a = 1 \\) so \\( a = \\frac{1}{2} \\)\n- \\( a + b + c = c + 2 \\)\n\nUsing \\( f(1) = 1 \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}(1)^2 + b(1) + c = 1 \\implies \\frac{1}{2} + b + c = 1 \\implies b + c = \\frac{1}{2}.\n\\]\n\nUsing \\( f(0) = -1 \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}(0)^2 + b(0) + c = -1 \\implies c = -1.\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( c = -1 \\) into \\( b + c = \\frac{1}{2} \\):\n\\[\nb - 1 = \\frac{1}{2} \\implies b = \\frac{3}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the function is:\n\\[\nf(x) = \\frac{1}{2}x^2 + \\frac{3}{2}x - 1.\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Find integers \\( n \\) such that \\( f(n) = n \\)\n\nSet \\( f(n) = n \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}n^2 + \\frac{3}{2}n - 1 = n.\n\\]\nSimplify:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}n^2 + \\frac{3}{2}n - 1 - n = 0 \\implies \\frac{1}{2}n^2 + \\frac{1}{2}n - 1 = 0.\n\\]\nMultiply by 2:\n\\[\nn^2 + n - 2 = 0.\n\\]\nFactor:\n\\[\n(n - 1)(n + 2) = 0.\n\\]\nThus, \\( n = 1 \\) or \\( n = -2 \\).\n\nThe integers \\( n \\) such that \\( f(n) = n \\) are \\(\\boxed{-2, 1}\\)."
'To compute the sum \\(\\sum_{n = 1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{F_n F_{n + 2}}\\), where \\(F_n\\) denotes the \\(n\\)th Fibonacci number, we start by examining the terms of the series.\n\nThe Fibonacci sequence is defined by \\(F_0 = 0\\), \\(F_1 = 1\\), and \\(F_{n} = F_{n-1} + F_{n-2}\\) for \\(n \\geq 2\\).\n\nWe can use the identity for Fibonacci numbers:\n\\[ F_{n+2} = F_{n+1} + F_n. \\]\n\nWe aim to express \\(\\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+2}}\\) in a telescoping form. Consider:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+2}} = \\frac{1}{F_n (F_{n+1} + F_n)} = \\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+1} + F_n^2}.\n\\]\n\nWe can rewrite this as:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+2}} = \\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+1}} - \\frac{1}{F_{n+1} F_{n+2}}.\n\\]\n\nThis decomposition is valid because:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+1}} - \\frac{1}{F_{n+1} F_{n+2}} = \\frac{F_{n+2} - F_n}{F_n F_{n+1} F_{n+2}} = \\frac{F_{n+1}}{F_n F_{n+1} F_{n+2}} = \\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+2}}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the series becomes:\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\left( \\frac{1}{F_n F_{n+1}} - \\frac{1}{F_{n+1} F_{n+2}} \\right).\n\\]\n\nThis is a telescoping series. Most terms cancel, leaving:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{F_1 F_2} = \\frac{1}{1 \\cdot 1} = 1.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of the series is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'Given that \\( x + y + z = 0 \\), we want to find the maximum possible value of \n\n\\[\n\\frac{xy + yz + zx}{x^2 + y^2 + z^2}.\n\\]\n\nFirst, we use the identity for the square of a sum:\n\n\\[\n(x + y + z)^2 = x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 2(xy + yz + zx).\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x + y + z = 0 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n0 = x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 2(xy + yz + zx).\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = -2(xy + yz + zx).\n\\]\n\nSubstituting this into the expression we want to maximize, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{xy + yz + zx}{x^2 + y^2 + z^2} = \\frac{xy + yz + zx}{-2(xy + yz + zx)} = -\\frac{1}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to a constant value of \\(-\\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\nTo verify that this is indeed achievable, consider specific values for \\( x, y, z \\). 'To find the sum of the quotient and remainder when \\(6x^3 + 9x^2 - 17x + 11\\) is divided by \\(2x^2 + 5x - 1\\), we perform polynomial long division.\n\n1. **Divide the leading terms**: Divide the leading term of the dividend, \\(6x^3\\), by the leading term of the divisor, \\(2x^2\\), to get the first term of the quotient: \n   \\[\n   \\frac{6x^3}{2x^2} = 3x.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Multiply and subtract**: Multiply the entire divisor \\(2x^2 + 5x - 1\\) by \\(3x\\) and subtract from the original polynomial:\n   \\[\n   (6x^3 + 9x^2 - 17x + 11) - (3x \\cdot (2x^2 + 5x - 1)) = (6x^3 + 9x^2 - 17x + 11) - (6x^3 + 15x^2 - 3x).\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   (6x^3 + 9x^2 - 17x + 11) - (6x^3 + 15x^2 - 3x) = -6x^2 - 14x + 11.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Repeat the process**: Divide the new leading term \\(-6x^2\\) by the leading term of the divisor \\(2x^2\\):\n   \\[\n   \\frac{-6x^2}{2x^2} = -3.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Multiply and subtract again**: Multiply the entire divisor by \\(-3\\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (-6x^2 - 14x + 11) - (-3 \\cdot (2x^2 + 5x - 1)) = (-6x^2 - 14x + 11) - (-6x^2 - 15x + 3).\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   (-6x^2 - 14x + 11) - (-6x^2 - 15x + 3) = x + 8.\n   \\]\n\nThe division process gives us a quotient of \\(3x - 3\\) and a remainder of \\(x + 8\\).\n\n5. **Sum the quotient and remainder**: The sum of the quotient and remainder is:\n   \\[\n   (3x - 3) + (x + 8) = 4x + 5.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the sum of the quotient and remainder is \\(\\boxed{4x + 5}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\log_{3x} 4 = \\log_{2x} 8\\), we start by expressing the logarithms in terms of the natural logarithm:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{3x} 4 = \\frac{\\ln 4}{\\ln (3x)}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\log_{2x} 8 = \\frac{\\ln 8}{\\ln (2x)}\n\\]\n\nSetting these two expressions equal gives:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\ln 4}{\\ln (3x)} = \\frac{\\ln 8}{\\ln (2x)}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying yields:\n\n\\[\n\\ln 4 \\cdot \\ln (2x) = \\ln 8 \\cdot \\ln (3x)\n\\]\n\nWe know that \\(\\ln 4 = 2\\ln 2\\) and \\(\\ln 8 = 3\\ln 2\\). Substituting these into the equation gives:\n\n\\[\n2\\ln 2 \\cdot \\ln (2x) = 3\\ln 2 \\cdot \\ln (3x)\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by \\(\\ln 2\\) (assuming \\(\\ln 2 \\neq 0\\)):\n\n\\[\n2 \\ln (2x) = 3 \\ln (3x)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the logarithms:\n\n\\[\n2 (\\ln 2 + \\ln x) = 3 (\\ln 3 + \\ln x)\n\\]\n\nDistribute the constants:\n\n\\[\n2\\ln 2 + 2\\ln x = 3\\ln 3 + 3\\ln x\n\\]\n\nRearrange to isolate terms involving \\(\\ln x\\):\n\n\\[\n2\\ln 2 - 3\\ln 3 = 3\\ln x - 2\\ln x\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n2\\ln 2 - 3\\ln 3 = \\ln x\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\ln x = 2\\ln 2 - 3\\ln 3\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\ln x = \\ln \\left(\\frac{2^2}{3^3}\\right)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{4}{27}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution to the equation is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{4}{27}}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the values of \\( N \\) such that the number of players given elite status is 19. The formula for the number of players given elite status is:\n\n\\[\n2^{1+\\lfloor \\log_{2} (N-1) \\rfloor} - N = 19\n\\]\n\nLet's denote \\( k = \\lfloor \\log_{2} (N-1) \\rfloor \\). 'To solve the inequality \\(\\frac{1}{x-1} - \\frac{1}{x-7} > 1\\), we first find a common denominator for the fractions on the left-hand side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x-1} - \\frac{1}{x-7} = \\frac{x-7 - (x-1)}{(x-1)(x-7)} = \\frac{-6}{(x-1)(x-7)}\n\\]\n\nThus, the inequality becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-6}{(x-1)(x-7)} > 1\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by \\((x-1)(x-7)\\), we must consider the sign of \\((x-1)(x-7)\\) to ensure the inequality direction is correct. We have two cases:\n\n1. \\((x-1)(x-7) > 0\\)\n2. \\((x-1)(x-7) < 0\\)\n\n**Case 1:** \\((x-1)(x-7) > 0\\)\n\nThis occurs when \\(x < 1\\) or \\(x > 7\\). In this case, multiplying by \\((x-1)(x-7)\\) does not change the inequality direction:\n\n\\[\n-6 > (x-1)(x-7)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right-hand side:\n\n\\[\n-6 > x^2 - 8x + 7\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 8x + 13 < 0\n\\]\n\nTo solve this quadratic inequality, we find the roots of the equation \\(x^2 - 8x + 13 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{8 \\pm \\sqrt{64 - 52}}{2} = \\frac{8 \\pm \\sqrt{12}}{2} = \\frac{8 \\pm 2\\sqrt{3}}{2} = 4 \\pm \\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\(x = 4 + \\sqrt{3}\\) and \\(x = 4 - \\sqrt{3}\\). The quadratic \\(x^2 - 8x + 13\\) is a parabola opening upwards, so it is negative between its roots:\n\n\\[\n4 - \\sqrt{3} < x < 4 + \\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\n**Case 2:** \\((x-1)(x-7) < 0\\)\n\nThis occurs when \\(1 < x < 7\\). In this case, multiplying by \\((x-1)(x-7)\\) reverses the inequality direction:\n\n\\[\n-6 < (x-1)(x-7)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right-hand side:\n\n\\[\n-6 < x^2 - 8x + 7\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 8x + 13 > 0\n\\]\n\nThe quadratic \\(x^2 - 8x + 13\\) is positive outside the interval \\((4 - \\sqrt{3}, 4 + \\sqrt{3})\\). However, since \\(1 < x < 7\\), we only consider the intervals where the quadratic is positive within this range:\n\n\\[\n1 < x < 4 - \\sqrt{3} \\quad \\text{or} \\quad 4 + \\sqrt{3} < x < 7\n\\]\n\nCombining the results from both cases, the solution to the inequality is:\n\n\\[\n(1, 4 - \\sqrt{3}) \\cup (4 + \\sqrt{3}, 7) \\cup (7, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{(1, 4 - \\sqrt{3}) \\cup (4 + \\sqrt{3}, 7) \\cup (7, \\infty)}\n\\]'
'To compute the product\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(1998^2 - 1996^2)(1998^2 - 1995^2) \\dotsm (1998^2 - 0^2)}{(1997^2 - 1996^2)(1997^2 - 1995^2) \\dotsm (1997^2 - 0^2)},\n\\]\n\nwe start by simplifying each term in the numerator and the denominator using the difference of squares formula:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a-b)(a+b).\n\\]\n\nFor the numerator, each term is of the form:\n\n\\[\n1998^2 - k^2 = (1998 - k)(1998 + k).\n\\]\n\nFor the denominator, each term is of the form:\n\n\\[\n1997^2 - k^2 = (1997 - k)(1997 + k).\n\\]\n\nThus, the product becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\prod_{k=0}^{1996} (1998-k)(1998+k)}{\\prod_{k=0}^{1996} (1997-k)(1997+k)}.\n\\]\n\nWe can separate this into two products:\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{k=0}^{1996} \\frac{1998-k}{1997-k} \\times \\prod_{k=0}^{1996} \\frac{1998+k}{1997+k}.\n\\]\n\nNow, consider each product separately:\n\n1. For \\(\\prod_{k=0}^{1996} \\frac{1998-k}{1997-k}\\):\n\n   - When \\(k = 0\\), the term is \\(\\frac{1998}{1997}\\).\n   - When \\(k = 1\\), the term is \\(\\frac{1997}{1996}\\).\n   - When \\(k = 2\\), the term is \\(\\frac{1996}{1995}\\).\n   - ...\n   - When \\(k = 1996\\), the term is \\(\\frac{2}{1}\\).\n\n   This product telescopes to:\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1998}{1}.\n   \\]\n\n2. For \\(\\prod_{k=0}^{1996} \\frac{1998+k}{1997+k}\\):\n\n   - When \\(k = 0\\), the term is \\(\\frac{1998}{1997}\\).\n   - When \\(k = 1\\), the term is \\(\\frac{1999}{1998}\\).\n   - When \\(k = 2\\), the term is \\(\\frac{2000}{1999}\\).\n   - ...\n   - When \\(k = 1996\\), the term is \\(\\frac{3994}{3993}\\).\n\n   This product telescopes to:\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{3994}{1997}.\n   \\]\n\nCombining these results, the entire product simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1998}{1} \\times \\frac{3994}{1997} = \\frac{1998 \\times 3994}{1997}.\n\\]\n\nSince \\(3994 = 2 \\times 1997\\), the expression simplifies further:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1998 \\times 2 \\times 1997}{1997} = 1998 \\times 2 = 3996.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the product is \\(\\boxed{3996}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( d \\) for the given ellipse, we need to understand the properties of an ellipse defined by the equation \\( PF_1 + PF_2 = d \\), where \\( F_1 \\) and \\( F_2 \\) are the foci of the ellipse.\n\nThe standard form of an ellipse centered at the origin with foci along the x-axis is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a \\) is the semi-major axis, \\( b \\) is the semi-minor axis, and the distance between the foci is \\( 2c \\) with \\( c = \\sqrt{a^2 - b^2} \\).\n\nThe sum of the distances from any point on the ellipse to the two foci is constant and equal to \\( 2a \\). Therefore, \\( d = 2a \\).\n\nFrom the diagram, we can see that the ellipse is centered at \\((-1, 0)\\) and has a horizontal major axis. The semi-major axis length \\( a \\) is 7, and the semi-minor axis length \\( b \\) is 5.\n\nThus, the value of \\( d \\) is:\n\n\\[\nd = 2a = 2 \\times 7 = 14\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( d \\) is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'
'To find the remainder when the polynomial \\( f(x) = x^{18} + x^{13} + x^7 + x^4 + x \\) is divided by \\( x^3 - x \\), we first note that \\( x^3 - x = x(x-1)(x+1) \\). This means the roots of \\( x^3 - x = 0 \\) are \\( x = 0, 1, -1 \\).\n\nThe remainder when dividing by \\( x^3 - x \\) will be a polynomial of degree less than 3, say \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\). We can find the coefficients \\( a, b, \\) and \\( c \\) by evaluating \\( f(x) \\) at the roots of \\( x^3 - x \\).\n\n1. **Evaluate at \\( x = 0 \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(0) = 0^{18} + 0^{13} + 0^7 + 0^4 + 0 = 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\( c = 0 \\).\n\n2. **Evaluate at \\( x = 1 \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^{18} + 1^{13} + 1^7 + 1^4 + 1 = 1 + 1 + 1 + 1 + 1 = 5\n   \\]\n   So, \\( a(1)^2 + b(1) + c = a + b + c = 5 \\).\n\n3. **Evaluate at \\( x = -1 \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^{18} + (-1)^{13} + (-1)^7 + (-1)^4 + (-1) = 1 - 1 - 1 + 1 - 1 = -1\n   \\]\n   So, \\( a(-1)^2 + b(-1) + c = a - b + c = -1 \\).\n\nNow we have the system of equations:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\na + b + c &= 5, \\\\\na - b + c &= -1, \\\\\nc &= 0.\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( c = 0 \\) into the first two equations, we get:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\na + b &= 5, \\\\\na - b &= -1.\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nAdding these two equations, we find:\n\\[\n2a = 4 \\implies a = 2.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( a = 2 \\) back into \\( a + b = 5 \\):\n\\[\n2 + b = 5 \\implies b = 3.\n\\]\n\nThus, the remainder is \\( 2x^2 + 3x + 0 \\), or simply \\( 2x^2 + 3x \\).\n\nTherefore, the remainder when \\( f(x) \\) is divided by \\( x^3 - x \\) is \\(\\boxed{2x^2 + 3x}\\).'
"The function \\( y = f(x) \\) is given as the natural logarithm function, \\( y = \\log(x) \\). The inverse of this function is the exponential function, \\( y = e^x \\).\n\nTo find the graph of \\( y = f^{-1}(x) \\), we need to reflect the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) over the line \\( y = x \\). This is because the graph of an inverse function is the reflection of the original function's graph over the line \\( y = x \\).\n\nLet's analyze the given options:\n\n- Graph A: This graph is a reflection over the line \\( y = x \\).\n- Graph B: This graph is a reflection over the line \\( y = -x \\).\n- Graph C: This graph is a reflection over the x-axis.\n- Graph D: This graph is a rotation of 180 degrees.\n- Graph E: This graph is a reflection over the line \\( y = x \\).\n\nBoth Graph A and Graph E are reflections over the line \\( y = x \\). However, upon closer inspection, Graph E is the correct reflection of the logarithmic function \\( y = \\log(x) \\) to produce the exponential function \\( y = e^x \\).\n\nTherefore, the correct graph of \\( y = f^{-1}(x) \\) is Graph E."
"To find the minimum value of \\(\\frac{1}{x} + y\\) given the constraint \\(x + \\frac{1}{y} = 5\\), we can use the method of Lagrange multipliers or algebraic manipulation. Here, we'll use algebraic manipulation.\n\nFirst, express \\(y\\) in terms of \\(x\\) using the constraint:\n\n\\[\nx + \\frac{1}{y} = 5 \\implies \\frac{1}{y} = 5 - x \\implies y = \\frac{1}{5-x}\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(y = \\frac{1}{5-x}\\) into the expression \\(\\frac{1}{x} + y\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} + y = \\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{5-x}\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum value, consider the function:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{5-x}\n\\]\n\nFind the derivative \\(f'(x)\\) and set it to zero to find critical points:\n\n\\[\nf'(x) = -\\frac{1}{x^2} + \\frac{1}{(5-x)^2}\n\\]\n\nSet \\(f'(x) = 0\\):\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{1}{x^2} + \\frac{1}{(5-x)^2} = 0 \\implies \\frac{1}{x^2} = \\frac{1}{(5-x)^2}\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = (5-x)^2\n\\]\n\nExpanding and solving for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 25 - 10x + x^2 \\implies 0 = 25 - 10x \\implies 10x = 25 \\implies x = 2.5\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(x = 2.5\\) back into the expression for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{5-x} = \\frac{1}{5-2.5} = \\frac{1}{2.5} = \\frac{2}{5}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(\\frac{1}{x} + y\\) at \\(x = 2.5\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} + y = \\frac{1}{2.5} + \\frac{2}{5} = \\frac{2}{5} + \\frac{2}{5} = \\frac{4}{5}\n\\]\n\nThus, the minimum value of \\(\\frac{1}{x} + y\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to find the relationship between the coefficients of the polynomials \\( f(x) \\) and \\( g(x) \\).\n\nGiven that \\( f(x) = x^3 + ax^2 + bx - 1 \\) has roots \\( r, s, t \\), by Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\\[\nr + s + t = -a,\n\\]\n\\[\nrs + rt + st = b,\n\\]\n\\[\nrst = 1.\n\\]\n\nThe polynomial \\( g(x) = x^3 + mx^2 + nx + p \\) has roots \\( r^2, s^2, t^2 \\). By Vieta's formulas for \\( g(x) \\), we have:\n\\[\nr^2 + s^2 + t^2 = -m,\n\\]\n\\[\nr^2s^2 + s^2t^2 + t^2r^2 = n,\n\\]\n\\[\nr^2s^2t^2 = p.\n\\]\n\nFirst, we calculate \\( r^2 + s^2 + t^2 \\):\n\\[\nr^2 + s^2 + t^2 = (r + s + t)^2 - 2(rs + rt + st) = a^2 - 2b.\n\\]\nThus, \\( m = -(r^2 + s^2 + t^2) = -(a^2 - 2b) = 2b - a^2 \\).\n\nNext, we calculate \\( r^2s^2 + s^2t^2 + t^2r^2 \\):\n\\[\nr^2s^2 + s^2t^2 + t^2r^2 = (rs + rt + st)^2 - 2rst(r + s + t) = b^2 - 2a.\n\\]\nThus, \\( n = b^2 - 2a \\).\n\nFinally, we calculate \\( r^2s^2t^2 \\):\n\\[\nr^2s^2t^2 = (rst)^2 = 1^2 = 1.\n\\]\nThus, \\( p = 1 \\).\n\nWe are given that \\( g(-1) = -5 \\). Therefore, substituting into \\( g(x) \\), we have:\n\\[\n(-1)^3 + m(-1)^2 + n(-1) + p = -5.\n\\]\nSimplifying, we get:\n\\[\n-1 + m - n + 1 = -5,\n\\]\n\\[\nm - n = -5.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the expressions for \\( m \\) and \\( n \\):\n\\[\n(2b - a^2) - (b^2 - 2a) = -5.\n\\]\nSimplifying, we have:\n\\[\n2b - a^2 - b^2 + 2a = -5.\n\\]\nRearranging terms, we get:\n\\[\n-b^2 + 2b + 2a - a^2 = -5.\n\\]\n\\[\nb^2 - 2b + a^2 - 2a = 5.\n\\]\n\nTo find the greatest possible value of \\( b \\), we complete the square for both \\( b \\) and \\( a \\):\n\\[\n(b - 1)^2 - 1 + (a - 1)^2 - 1 = 5,\n\\]\n\\[\n(b - 1)^2 + (a - 1)^2 = 7.\n\\]\n\nThe maximum value of \\( b \\) occurs when \\( b - 1 \\) is maximized, which happens when \\( a - 1 = 0 \\). Thus, \\( a = 1 \\), and:\n\\[\n(b - 1)^2 = 7,\n\\]\n\\[\nb - 1 = \\sqrt{7} \\quad \\text{or} \\quad b - 1 = -\\sqrt{7}.\n\\]\n\nThe greatest possible value of \\( b \\) is:\n\\[\nb = 1 + \\sqrt{7}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the greatest possible value for \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{1 + \\sqrt{7}}\\)."
'To simplify the fraction \\(\\frac{8x^3 + 27y^3}{2x + 3y}\\), we recognize that the numerator is a sum of cubes. The sum of cubes formula is:\n\n\\[\na^3 + b^3 = (a + b)(a^2 - ab + b^2)\n\\]\n\nIn this case, we have \\(a = 2x\\) and \\(b = 3y\\), so:\n\n\\[\n(2x)^3 + (3y)^3 = 8x^3 + 27y^3 = (2x + 3y)((2x)^2 - (2x)(3y) + (3y)^2)\n\\]\n\nCalculating the terms inside the second factor:\n\n\\[\n(2x)^2 = 4x^2, \\quad (2x)(3y) = 6xy, \\quad (3y)^2 = 9y^2\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n8x^3 + 27y^3 = (2x + 3y)(4x^2 - 6xy + 9y^2)\n\\]\n\nNow, we can simplify the original fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{8x^3 + 27y^3}{2x + 3y} = \\frac{(2x + 3y)(4x^2 - 6xy + 9y^2)}{2x + 3y}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(2x + 3y\\) is a common factor in the numerator and the denominator, they cancel out, leaving:\n\n\\[\n4x^2 - 6xy + 9y^2\n\\]\n\nThis expression is in the form \\(ax^2 + bxy + cy^2\\) where \\(a = 4\\), \\(b = -6\\), and \\(c = 9\\). "To solve the expression \\(1 - 3 + 5 - 7 + 9 - \\cdots - 43 + 45 - 47 + 49\\), we first observe the pattern of the sequence. The sequence alternates between adding and subtracting consecutive odd numbers.\n\nLet's break down the sequence into pairs:\n\n\\[\n(1 - 3), (5 - 7), (9 - 11), \\ldots, (45 - 47), 49\n\\]\n\nEach pair \\((a - b)\\) can be simplified as:\n\n\\[\na - b = (2n - 1) - (2n + 1) = -2\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = 2n - 1\\) and \\(b = 2n + 1\\).\n\nNow, let's count the number of such pairs. 'The product of an even function and an odd function is an odd function. \n\nTo see why, consider the definitions of even and odd functions:\n\n- A function \\( f(x) \\) is even if \\( f(-x) = f(x) \\) for all \\( x \\).\n- A function \\( g(x) \\) is odd if \\( g(-x) = -g(x) \\) for all \\( x \\).\n\nNow, consider the product \\( h(x) = f(x)g(x) \\). We have:\n\n\\[ h(-x) = f(-x)g(-x) = f(x)(-g(x)) = -f(x)g(x) = -h(x). \\]\n\nThis shows that \\( h(x) \\) satisfies the condition for being an odd function. Therefore, the product \\( f(x)g(x) \\) is "odd".'
"To find the minimum value of the expression\n\n\\[\n\\left\\lfloor \\frac{b + c + d}{a} \\right\\rfloor + \\left\\lfloor \\frac{a + c + d}{b} \\right\\rfloor + \\left\\lfloor \\frac{a + b + d}{c} \\right\\rfloor + \\left\\lfloor \\frac{a + b + c}{d} \\right\\rfloor,\n\\]\n\nwe start by considering the properties of the floor function. The floor function \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) gives the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\).\n\nTo minimize the sum of these floor functions, we need to make each fraction as small as possible while ensuring that the sum of the floors is minimized. 'To solve the problem, we start by setting up the equations based on the given conditions. We have two different positive numbers \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) such that each differs from its reciprocal by 1. This gives us the equations:\n\n\\[\na - \\frac{1}{a} = 1\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb - \\frac{1}{b} = 1\n\\]\n\nWe will solve each equation separately.\n\n**Solving for \\( a \\):**\n\nStarting with the equation for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\na - \\frac{1}{a} = 1\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by \\( a \\) to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[\na^2 - 1 = a\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\n\\[\na^2 - a - 1 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation. We can solve it using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -1 \\), and \\( c = -1 \\). Plugging in these values, we get:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4}}{2} = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions for \\( a \\) are:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\quad \\text{or} \\quad a = \\frac{1 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( a \\) is positive, we choose:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n**Solving for \\( b \\):**\n\nSimilarly, for \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nb - \\frac{1}{b} = 1\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 1 = b\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - b - 1 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is the same quadratic equation as for \\( a \\), so the solutions are:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\quad \\text{or} \\quad b = \\frac{1 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( b \\) is different from \\( a \\) and both are positive, we choose:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{1 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n**Finding \\( a + b \\):**\n\nNow, we find \\( a + b \\):\n\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} + \\frac{1 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{(1 + \\sqrt{5}) + (1 - \\sqrt{5})}{2} = \\frac{2}{2} = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the maximum value of \\(PQ + F_1Q\\), where \\(P\\) is a point on the circle \\(x^2 + (y - 3)^2 = 4\\) and \\(Q\\) is a point on the ellipse \\(\\frac{x^2}{49} + \\frac{y^2}{33} = 1\\).\n\nFirst, let's identify the foci of the ellipse. The standard form of the ellipse is \\(\\frac{x^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1\\), where \\(a^2 = 49\\) and \\(b^2 = 33\\). Since \\(a^2 > b^2\\), the foci are located on the x-axis at \\((\\pm c, 0)\\), where \\(c = \\sqrt{a^2 - b^2} = \\sqrt{49 - 33} = \\sqrt{16} = 4\\). Thus, the foci are \\(F_1 = (4, 0)\\) and \\(F_2 = (-4, 0)\\).\n\nThe circle \\(x^2 + (y - 3)^2 = 4\\) is centered at \\((0, 3)\\) with radius 2. A point \\(P\\) on this circle can be parameterized as \\(P = (2\\cos\\theta, 3 + 2\\sin\\theta)\\).\n\nThe line \\(F_2P\\) intersects the ellipse again at \\(Q\\). We need to find the maximum value of \\(PQ + F_1Q\\).\n\nThe key insight is to use the reflection property of ellipses: for any point \\(Q\\) on the ellipse, the sum of the distances from the foci is constant and equal to the major axis length, \\(2a = 14\\). Therefore, for any point \\(Q\\) on the ellipse, \\(F_1Q + F_2Q = 14\\).\n\nTo maximize \\(PQ + F_1Q\\), we note that \\(PQ + F_1Q = PQ + (14 - F_2Q) = 14 + (PQ - F_2Q)\\). Thus, we need to maximize \\(PQ - F_2Q\\).\n\nThe maximum value of \\(PQ - F_2Q\\) occurs when \\(P\\) and \\(Q\\) are collinear with \\(F_2\\), and \\(Q\\) is as far from \\(F_2\\) as possible. This happens when \\(Q\\) is at the endpoint of the major axis of the ellipse, which is \\((7, 0)\\).\n\nFor \\(P = (0, 5)\\), the line \\(F_2P\\) is vertical, and it intersects the ellipse at \\(Q = (7, 0)\\). In this case, \\(PQ = \\sqrt{(7 - 0)^2 + (0 - 5)^2} = \\sqrt{49 + 25} = \\sqrt{74}\\), and \\(F_1Q = 3\\).\n\nThus, the maximum value of \\(PQ + F_1Q\\) is \\(\\sqrt{74} + 3\\).\n\nTherefore, the maximum value of \\(PQ + F_1Q\\) is \\(\\boxed{14}\\)."
'To solve the problem, we start by simplifying the expression inside the sum:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{(\\sqrt{n} + \\sqrt{n+1})(\\sqrt[4]{n} + \\sqrt[4]{n+1})}.\n\\]\n\nFirst, consider the term \\((\\sqrt{n} + \\sqrt{n+1})\\). We can simplify this by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{n+1} - \\sqrt{n}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives:\n\n\\[\n(\\sqrt{n+1} - \\sqrt{n})(\\sqrt{n} + \\sqrt{n+1}) = (\\sqrt{n+1})^2 - (\\sqrt{n})^2 = n+1 - n = 1.\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{n+1} - \\sqrt{n}}{\\sqrt[4]{n} + \\sqrt[4]{n+1}}.\n\\]\n\nNext, consider the term \\((\\sqrt[4]{n} + \\sqrt[4]{n+1})\\). We can simplify this by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[4]{n+1} - \\sqrt[4]{n}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives:\n\n\\[\n(\\sqrt[4]{n+1} - \\sqrt[4]{n})(\\sqrt[4]{n} + \\sqrt[4]{n+1}) = (\\sqrt[4]{n+1})^2 - (\\sqrt[4]{n})^2 = \\sqrt{n+1} - \\sqrt{n}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{\\sqrt[4]{n+1} - \\sqrt[4]{n}}.\n\\]\n\nNow, the sum becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=1}^{9999} \\frac{1}{\\sqrt[4]{n+1} - \\sqrt[4]{n}}.\n\\]\n\nThis is a telescoping series. The terms will cancel out, leaving only the first and last terms. Specifically, the sum simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[4]{10000} - \\sqrt[4]{1} = 10 - 1 = 9.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of the sum is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to consider polynomials \\( P(z) = 4z^4 + az^3 + bz^2 + cz + d \\) with integer coefficients \\( a, b, c, d \\) such that \\( 0 \\leq d \\leq c \\leq b \\leq a \\leq 4 \\) and the polynomial has a zero \\( z_0 \\) with \\( |z_0| = 1 \\).\n\nGiven that \\( |z_0| = 1 \\), we have \\( z_0 \\overline{z_0} = 1 \\). If \\( z_0 \\) is a root, then \\( \\overline{z_0} \\) is also a root because the coefficients are real. Therefore, the polynomial can be expressed as:\n\n\\[\nP(z) = 4(z - z_0)(z - \\overline{z_0})(z - \\alpha)(z - \\beta)\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( \\alpha \\) and \\( \\beta \\) are the other roots. Since \\( |z_0| = 1 \\), we have \\( z_0 = e^{i\\theta} \\) for some real \\(\\theta\\), and thus \\( \\overline{z_0} = e^{-i\\theta} \\).\n\nThe condition \\( |z_0| = 1 \\) implies that the polynomial satisfies the condition \\( P(z) = z^4 \\overline{P(1/\\overline{z})} \\). Evaluating this at \\( z = 1 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nP(1) = 4(1)^4 + a(1)^3 + b(1)^2 + c(1) + d = 4 + a + b + c + d\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the sum of all possible values of \\( P(1) \\) given the constraints on \\( a, b, c, \\) and \\( d \\).\n\nThe constraints \\( 0 \\leq d \\leq c \\leq b \\leq a \\leq 4 \\) imply that \\( a, b, c, \\) and \\( d \\) can take values from 0 to 4, but each must be less than or equal to the previous one. We can count the number of solutions to this inequality using the "stars and bars" method or by direct enumeration.\n\nFor each valid tuple \\((a, b, c, d)\\), we compute \\( P(1) = 4 + a + b + c + d \\). The sum of all such values is equivalent to summing over all possible values of \\( a, b, c, \\) and \\( d \\) that satisfy the constraints.\n\nTo find the sum, we consider the generating function approach. The generating function for each variable is:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = 1 + x + x^2 + x^3 + x^4 = \\frac{1-x^5}{1-x}\n\\]\n\nThe generating function for the sum \\( a + b + c + d \\) is:\n\n\\[\n(f(x))^4 = \\left(\\frac{1-x^5}{1-x}\\right)^4\n\\]\n\nWe are interested in the coefficient of \\( x^k \\) in the expansion of this generating function, where \\( k \\) is the sum of the indices. The sum of all values of \\( P(1) \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{a=0}^{4} \\sum_{b=0}^{a} \\sum_{c=0}^{b} \\sum_{d=0}^{c} (4 + a + b + c + d)\n\\]\n\nThis is equivalent to evaluating the generating function at \\( x = 1 \\) and multiplying by the number of terms. The number of terms is the number of non-decreasing sequences of length 4 with elements from 0 to 4, which is given by the binomial coefficient \\(\\binom{4+4}{4} = 70\\).\n\nThus, the sum of all values of \\( P(1) \\) is:\n\n\\[\n70 \\times (4 + \\text{average of } a + b + c + d)\n\\]\n\nThe average value of \\( a + b + c + d \\) is the expected value of the sum of four independent uniform random variables each taking values from 0 to 4, which is \\( 2 \\times 4 = 8 \\).\n\nTherefore, the sum of all values of \\( P(1) \\) is:\n\n\\[\n70 \\times (4 + 8) = 70 \\times 12 = 840\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of all values \\( P(1) \\) over all the polynomials with these properties is \\(\\boxed{840}\\).'
